Cotton Use in Ghusl: Al-Zayla'i vs. the Majority
Intra-madhhab dispute on cotton use for the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on using cotton for the deceased and state the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Cotton may be used in all orifices except the private parts, according to the relied Hanafi position.

Preparing the deceased (ghusl) involves careful handling of the body. One practical question is whether cotton can be used to stuff orifices. This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam al-Zayla'i and the majority of earlier scholars, refining your understanding of how later authorities resolved the issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing views
The passage first notes that the apparent narrations (zahir al-riwaya) do not mention using cotton at all. Then it presents al-Zayla'i's permission for all orifices, followed by the majority's dislike (istiqbah) for the anus and front private part.
The 'majority' refers to the mashayikh cited in al-Dhahiriyyah.
2
Analyze the basis of each view
Al-Zayla'i's view appears pragmatic: cotton helps absorb fluids and maintain dignity. The majority's dislike likely stems from heightened reverence for the private parts (awrah).
The text does not cite explicit proofs; the disagreement is one of ihtiyat (precaution) vs. practicality.
3
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Later Hanafi jurists, including al-Tahtawi, adopt al-Zayla'i's permissive stance for non-private orifices, but uphold the majority's dislike for the private parts. Thus the relied position: cotton is permissible everywhere except the anus and front private part, where it is makruh tanzih.
This is a classic tarjih between a later authority and earlier majority.
4
Identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, a Hanafi may use cotton for the mouth, nose, and ears without any dislike, but should avoid the anus and front private part if possible, or at least be aware of the dislike.
The difference affects the degree of sin/reward, not validity of the ghusl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس في الغسل استعمال القطن في الروايات الظاهرة وقال الزيلعي : لا بأس بأن يجعل القطن على وجهه وأن يحشى به مخارقه كالدبر والقبل والأذنين، والأنف والفم انتهى، وفي الظهيرية واستقبح عامة المشايخ جعله في دبره أو قبله
And there is no use of cotton in ghusl in the apparent narrations. Al-Zayla'i said: there is no harm in placing cotton on his face and stuffing his openings like the anus, front private part, ears, nose, and mouth. And in al-Dhahiriyyah, the majority of scholars considered making it in his anus or front private part as reprehensible.
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-madhhab dispute regarding the use of cotton when washing the deceased. The apparent (zahir) narrations from the Hanafi school indicate that cotton is not used at all. However, Imam al-Zayla'i, a later Hanafi authority, opines that it is permissible to place cotton on the face and to fill the various orifices, including the anus, front private part, ears, nose, and mouth. This view is more accommodating. On the other hand, the text from al-Dhahiriyyah reports that the majority of early Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) considered using cotton specifically in the anus or front private part as reprehensible (mustaqbah). This indicates that while cotton use in other areas may be acceptable, the private parts are treated with greater reverence. The mufta bihi position today leans towards permissibility of cotton in orifices except the private parts, as stated by al-Zayla'i, given that the later scholars (mutakkhirin) often preferred this view for practical reasons.

Key Terms
مخارقه (makhariq): Openings or orifices of the body, such as the anus, front private part, ears, nose, and mouth.
استقبح (istaqbaha): Considered reprehensible (makruh tanzih).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Dhahiriyyah, where is cotton use considered reprehensible?
A) In the mouth
B) In the ears
C) In the anus or front private part
D) On the face

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that using cotton for the deceased is generally permissible, but it is disliked (makruh tanzih) in the anus and front private part, per the majority view adopted by later authorities.

Ruling on Cutting Nails and Hair of the Deceased
Ruling on the prohibition of cutting nails and hair of the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting nails and hair of the deceased and explain the reasoning based on the absence of need for adornment.

Core Idea
Cutting a deceased's nails or hair is haram because it is an act of beautification for the living, and the dead are free from such needs.

This lesson covers the first ruling from the passage: the prohibition of cutting the nails or hair of a deceased person. The text clarifies that such actions are considered adornment, which the deceased no longer requires. Understanding this ruling helps us recognize the respectful treatment of the deceased in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Notice that the text explicitly prohibits cutting nails, hair, and combing. The ruling is haram (prohibited).
The prohibition is general; a broken nail is an exception but not mentioned here.
2
Understand the reason
The text states it is 'because it is for adornment and he has become free of it'. The deceased no longer needs beautification.
This reason distinguishes the dead from the living who are encouraged to groom.
3
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school allows cutting nails and hair, considering the dead to be like the living in this respect.
The Hanafi position relies on the absence of need as the operative cause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقص ظفره) أي الميت (و) لا (شعره ولا يسرح شعره أي شعر رأسه ولحيته) لأنه للزينة وقد استغنى عنها (والمرأة تغسل زوجها ولو معتدة من رجعي أو ظهار منها في الأظهر أو إلى ما لا يحل مسه، والنظر إليه ببقاء العدة فلو ولدت عقب موته وانقضت عدتها من رجعي أو كانت مبانة، أو
And his nail is not cut, nor his hair, nor is his hair of head and beard combed, because it is for adornment and he has become free of it. And the woman washes her husband even if she is in an irrevocable divorce iddah or a zihar from her in the apparent view, or till what is not permissible to touch and look at due to remaining iddah, so if she gives birth after his death and her iddah from an irrevocable divorce ends, or she was divorced irrevocably, or...
Source pages p. 571

Commentary
This passage states two clear rulings. First, it is prohibited to cut the deceased's nails or hair, or to comb the hair, because these are acts of beautification for the living, and the dead no longer need them. However, if a nail is broken, it may be removed. Second, a woman may wash her husband's body after death, even if she is in the iddah period of a revocable divorce (raj'i) or after zihar (a type of divorce-like oath). The reason is that the marriage bond still partially exists during revocable iddah, so physical contact is allowed. If she is in an irrevocable divorce (ba'in) or has given birth and completed iddah, she may not wash him. The Hanafi school holds that the marital relationship continues for purposes of ghusl during revocable iddah.

Key Terms
رجعي (raj'i): A revocable divorce where the husband can take back his wife without a new marriage.
ظهار (zihar): A husband saying to his wife 'You are to me like my mother's back', which requires expiation before resuming relations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on cutting the nails of a deceased person?
A) It is recommended
B) It is haram
C) It is permissible only if the nails are long
D) It is required before burial

Key Takeaway
Cutting the deceased's nails or hair is haram because the dead do not need adornment.

Ruling on Wife Washing Her Deceased Husband
Ruling on wife washing deceased husband based on iddah status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine when a woman may wash her deceased husband according to the Hanafi school, distinguishing between revocable and irrevocable divorce iddah.

Core Idea
A woman may wash her deceased husband if she is in revocable iddah; otherwise, it is not permitted.

This lesson examines the second ruling from the passage: the permissibility for a woman to wash the body of her deceased husband. The Hanafi school allows this when the marriage bond is still considered intact, i.e., during revocable divorce iddah or after zihar, but not after irrevocable divorce or completion of iddah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The text states that a woman may wash her husband, even if she is in iddah of a revocable divorce or zihar. This establishes a general permissibility.
The permissibility is based on the continuity of the marriage bond.
2
Note the exception
The text then implies that if the iddah is from an irrevocable divorce (ba'in) or has ended, she may not wash him. This is deduced from the phrase 'due to remaining iddah'.
The ruling is conditional; the condition is that the marriage is still partially valid.
3
Apply to scenarios
Practice with: wife in raj'i iddah: allowed; wife in ba'in iddah: not allowed; wife after iddah completion: not allowed.
Zihar is treated like revocable divorce because the marriage is not completely dissolved.

Rulings of the Shroud (Kafan) for Men and Women
Detailed commentary on the proper shroud, its materials, and wrapping order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah shroud pieces for men and women, explain why the turban is makruh, and apply the correct wrapping order.

Core Idea
Men's sunnah shroud: 3 pieces; women's: 5. The turban is makruh. White cotton is preferred.

The shroud (kafan) is a sunnah covering for the deceased, with specific pieces and materials rooted in the Prophet's practice. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling on the number of pieces, the disliked turban, and the proper wrapping order, drawing on hadith and the school's authoritative texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling level
Determine whether the shroud is fard, wajib, or sunnah. The text states it is sunnah muakkadah, with a sufficient minimum (kifayah) allowed when needed.
The minimum to cover the 'awrah is fard, but the full sunnah shroud is recommended.
2
List the sunnah pieces for a man
From the text: a man's sunnah shroud consists of three pieces: izār (loincloth), qamīṣ (shirt), and lifāfah (wrapper). The turban is not included and is disliked.
The qamīṣ must not have sleeves, pocket, or front slit.
3
List the sunnah pieces for a woman
A woman's sunnah shroud consists of five pieces: dir' (chemise), izār, khimār (head covering), khirqah (cloth between breasts and navel), and lifāfah.
The khirqah prevents exposure during carrying. The sufficient shroud for a woman is three pieces.
4
Understand the wrapping order and tying
The lifāfah is spread, then izār on top, then the deceased in the qamīṣ. The izār is folded from left side then right, similarly the lifāfah. The shroud is tied if needed to prevent unwrapping.
The right side is kept higher by analogy with the living.
5
Resolve the turban dispute
The turban is makruh tanzih in the soundest view because the Prophet's shroud did not include it. Some later scholars permitted it based on Ibn Umar's practice, but the mufta bihi is dislike.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للرجل إزار ولفافة) في الأصح مع قلة المال وكثرة الورثة هو أولى، وعلى القلب كفن السنة أولى وفضل البياض من القطن لما روينا والخلق الغسيل والجديد فيه سواء (وكل من الإزار واللفافة للميت يكون من القرن) يعني شعر الرأس (إلى القدم) الزيادة للربط (ولا يجعل لقميصه كم لأنه لحاجة الحي (ولا دخر يص) لا يفعل إلا للحي ليتسع الأسفل للمشي فيه ولا جيب) وهو الشق النازل على الصدر لأنه لحاجة الحي ولو كفن في قميص حي قطع جيبه ولبنته وكميه ولا تكف أطرافه لعدم الحاجة إليه وتكره العمامة في الأصح لأنها لم تكن في كفن النبي ، واستحسنها بعضهم لما روي أن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما كان يعممه، ويجعل العذبة على وجهه (و) تبسط اللفافة، ثم الإزار فوقها ثم يوضع الميت مقمصاً : ثم يعطف عليه الإزار و(لف) الإزار (من جهة) (يساره ثم من جهة (يمينه) ليكون اليمين أعلى، ثم فعل باللفافة كذلك اعتباراً بحالة الحياة (وعقد) الكفن (إن خيف انتشاره) صيانة للميت عن الكشف وتزاد المرأة على ما ذكرناه للرجل (في) كفنها على جهة السنة) خماراً لوجهها) ورأسها (وخرقة) رضها ما بين الثدي إلى السرة، وقيل: إلى الركبة كي لا ينتشر الكفن بالفخذ وقت المشي بها التربط ثدييها) فسنة كفنها درع وإزار وخمار وخرقة ولفافة (و) تزاد المرأة (في) كفن (الكفاية) على كفن الرجل (خماراً) فيكون ثلاثة خمار ولفافة وإزار ( ويجعل شعرها ضفيرتين) وتوضعان على صدرها فوق القميص ثم يوضع (الخمار) على رأسها ووجهها (فوقه) أي القميص فيكون (تحت اللفافة ثم) تربط (الخرقة فوقها لئلا تنتشر الأكفان وتعطف من اليسار ثم من اليمين وتجمر الأكفان) للرجل والمرأة جميعاً مجميراً وتراً قبل أن يدرج) الميت (فيها) لقوله : «إذا أجمرتم تجميراً وتراً)
For the man: a loincloth and a wrapper. In the soundest view, when wealth is little and heirs many, the sufficient shroud is better. In contrast, the sunnah shroud is better. And white (cloth) from cotton is preferred, as we have transmitted. And old washed (cloth) and new are equal in it. And both the loincloth and the wrapper for the deceased must be from the crown (meaning hair of the head) to the foot; the excess is for tying. And one should not make sleeves for his shirt, because it is for the need of the living. And no pocket (dyke?) – it is made only for the living so that the bottom expands for walking. And no slit (jayb), which is the opening descending on the chest, because it is for the need of the living. If he shrouded in a living person's shirt, he cuts its slit, its ornamental piece (labbah), and its sleeves. And he does not fold its edges due to lack of need. And the turban is disliked in the soundest view, because it was not in the shroud of the Prophet (PBUH). And some scholars considered it good due to what was related that Ibn Umar (RA) used to turban it and put the end (al-udhbah) on his face. And the wrapper is spread, then the loincloth on top of it, then the deceased is placed wearing the shirt, then the loincloth is folded over him. And the loincloth is folded from his left side, then from his right side, so that the right is higher. Then the same is done with the wrapper, by analogy with the state of life. And the shroud is tied if its spreading is feared, to protect the deceased from exposure. And the woman is given extra beyond what we mentioned for the man, in her shroud according to the sunnah: a head covering (khimar) for her face and head, and a cloth (khirqah) from between the breasts to the navel – and it is said to the knee – so that the shroud does not spread over the thigh during carrying her; and (the cloth) binds her breasts. So the sunnah of her shroud is: a chemise (dir'), a loincloth, a head covering, a cloth (khirqah), and a wrapper. And the woman is given extra in the sufficient shroud over the man's shroud: a head covering, so it becomes three: head covering, wrapper, and loincloth. And her hair is made into two braids, and they are placed on her chest above the shirt. Then the head covering is placed on her head and face above it (i.e., the shirt), so it is under the wrapper. Then the cloth (khirqah) is tied over it so that the shrouds do not spread. And it is folded from the left then from the right. And the shrouds are perfumed (tujammar) for both man and woman, with an odd number of perfumings, before the deceased is inserted into them, due to his saying: 'When you perfume, perfume an odd number of times.'
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi is a super-commentary (hāshiyah) on Marāqī al-Falāḥ, expanding on the rulings of the shroud (kaffān) for the deceased. It opens by presenting a core ruling: for a man, the minimum sufficient shroud is an izār (loincloth) and a lifāfah (wrapper) when wealth is limited and heirs are many, but the sunnah (recommended) shroud is superior. The author then details preferred materials: white cotton is best, based on the hadith that the Prophet (PBUH) was shrouded in three white cotton garments. Old but washed cloth is equal to new, as narrated from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq. Each piece must cover from the head (crown) to the feet, with extra length for tying. The shirt (qamīṣ) should lack sleeves (kumm), a pocket (jab?—unclear), and a front slit (jayb) because these serve the living's needs. If one uses a living person's shirt, these features must be cut off. The turban (imāmah) is deemed makrūh tanzīhan in the soundest view, as the Prophet's shroud lacked it, though some later scholars (mutā'akhkhirūn) allowed it based on Ibn Umar's practice. The wrapping order is then described: spread the lifāfah, then the izār on top, place the deceased in the shirt (muqammaṣ), fold the izār starting from the left side then the right (so the right is higher), then similarly wrap the lifāfah—all by analogy with the living's preference for the right. Tying is permitted if needed to prevent unwrapping. For women, the sunnah adds: a khimār (head covering), a khirqah (cloth from chest to navel or knee to prevent exposure), and a cloth to bind the breasts. Thus the sunnah set for a woman is five pieces: dir' (chemise), izār, khimār, khirqah, and lifāfah. For sufficiency (kifāyah), she needs three: khimār, lifāfah, izār. Her hair is braided and placed on her chest under the khimār. Finally, the shrouds should be perfumed (tajmīr) with incense an odd number of times before wrapping, following the Prophet's instruction. All these details reflect the Hanafi school's emphasis on emulating the sunnah while permitting necessity-based leniency.

Key Terms
إزار (izār): A lower garment covering from waist to shin; in kafan context, the cloth covering from navel to knees or feet.
لفافة (lifāfah): The outer wrapper that covers the entire body, from head to foot.
قميص (qamīṣ): A shirt-like garment covering the upper body, part of the sunnah shroud for men.
خمار (khimār): A head covering for women, covering the head and face.
خرقة (khirqah): A piece of cloth placed between the breasts and the navel (or knee) to prevent exposure during carrying.
جيب (jayb): The front opening/placket of a shirt; cut off in a shroud as it serves the living.
عمامة (imāmah): Turban; disliked in kafan because not part of Prophet's practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For a woman, how many pieces are considered the sunnah shroud according to this commentary?
A) Two: izār and lifāfah
B) Three: khimār, lifāfah, izār
C) Five: dir', izār, khimār, khirqah, lifāfah
D) Six: adding a turban

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah shroud for men is three pieces, for women five; the turban is makruh, and white cotton is preferred.

Salah — Prayer

6 min
The Funeral Prayer: Communal Obligation and its Pillars
Ruling that funeral prayer is fard kifayah and its arkan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the funeral prayer is fard kifayah, list its pillars according to the Hanafi school, and explain why wudu is not required after washing the deceased.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer is a communal obligation; the Prophet's leaving it shows it is not individual.

This lesson establishes the legal status of the funeral prayer as a communal obligation (fard kifayah) and outlines its essential components. Understanding this classification is crucial for fulfilling the community's duty toward the deceased. The passage also clarifies a common misconception regarding ritual purity after handling the deceased.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal classification
Recognize that the funeral prayer is fard kifayah (communal obligation), not fard 'ayn. This means that if a sufficient number of Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved; if none do, all sin.
2
Understand the evidence for fard kifayah
Note the proofs: the Quranic verse 'And pray for them' (9:103) and the Prophet's command 'Pray over every righteous and sinner'. The fact that the Prophet omitted it in some cases (e.g., when the deceased owed debt) shows it is not individually obligatory.
Denial of this consensus is kufr.
3
List the pillars (arkan) of the funeral prayer
The essential pillars are: intention (niyyah), four takbirs, standing (if able), and the final salam. Recitations (Fatiha, salawat, dua) are wajib, not rukn.
Omission of any rukn invalidates the prayer.
4
Note the ruling on wudu after washing the deceased
The Hanafi position is that wudu is not required after carrying, washing, or shrouding the deceased. Any hadith commanding it is interpreted as recommendation or precaution.
This is the view of Abu Hanifa, agreed upon by Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
5
Appreciate the wisdom behind the ruling
The wisdom is that handling the deceased causes fatigue, and wudu would invigorate; it is not an obligation but a recommended readiness for prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الصلاة عليه ككفنه ودفنه وتجهيزه فرض كفاية مع عدم الإنفراد بالخطاب بها ولو امرأة وأركانها لا وضوء على من حمل جنازة ولا على من حنط ميتاً، أو كفنه أو غسله، وهو قول أبي حنيفة كذا في الآثار له قال شارحه المثلا على وما ورد من الأمر بذلك محمول على الاحتياط، أو على من لا تكون له طهارة ليكون مستعداً للصلاة، فلا يفوته شيء منها ا هـ، وقيل الحكمة في ذلك أن مباشر الميت يحصل له فتور والوضوء والغسل ينشطه. قوله: (غفر له سبعون مغفرة) المراد التكثير كما قيل به في نظائره والمراد أن لا يبقى عليه من الذنوب شيء، وذلك دليل رضا الله تعالى على فالعه قوله: (قال) يقول الخ) فيه دليل على أن ذكر الله حال الغسل لا يكره، و الله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم. فصل هو بالتنوين لما فرغ من الغسل، والكفن شرع في الصلاة عليه إذ الشرط يتقدم على المشروط. قوله: (فرض) (كفاية بالإجماع فيكفر منكرها لإنكاره الإجماع كذا في البدائع، والقنية والأصل فيه قوله تعالى: (وصل عليهم) [التوبة: ٩] وقوله: صلوا على كل بر وفاجر وإنما كانت فرض كفاية لقوله صلوا على صاحبكم ولو كانت فرض عين ما تركها ولأن في الإيجاب العيني على الجميع استحالة وحرجاً فاكتفي بالبعض حموي، والجماعة فيها ليست بشرط والصلاة على الكبير أفضل منها على الصغير قهستاني، ويصح النذر بها لأنها قربة مقصودة بخلاف التكفين وتشييع الجنازة بحر قيل هي من خصائص هذه الأمة كالوصية بالثلث ورد بما أخرجه الحاكم وصححه عنه والله أنه قال: «كان آدم رجلاً أشقر طوالاً كأنه نخلة سحوق فلما حضره الموت نزلت الملائكة بحنوطه، وكفنه من الجنة فلما مات عليه الصلاة والسلام غسلوه بالماء والسدر ثلاثاً، وجعلوا في الثالثة كافوراً، وكفنوه في وتر من الثياب وحفروا له لحداً وصلوا عليه وقالوا لولده هذه سنة لمن بعده» فإن الخصوصية تعين حمله على أنه بالنسبة لمجرد التكبير والكيفية قال الواقدي: لم تكن شرعت يوم موت خديجة، وموتها رضي الله عنها بعد النبوة بعشر سنين على الأصح، وقوله وحفروا له لحداً أي بمكة عند حواء عليهما السلام كما ذكره ابن العماد وهو أحد أقوال، وكان جبريل هو الإمام بالملائكة كذا في النهاية وجزم ابن العماد بأنه شيث، ويمكن الجمع كما ذكره
Section: Prayer upon him (the deceased). Like his shrouding, burial, and preparation, it is a communal obligation (fard kifayah), with no individual address (to everyone), even for a woman. Its pillars: There is no wudu upon one who carried a bier, nor upon one who embalmed a deceased, or shrouded him, or washed him. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa. The commentary says: What is reported of the command [to do wudu] is interpreted as precaution or for one who does not have purity to be ready for prayer so as not to miss it. It is said the wisdom is that the one directly handling the deceased feels fatigue, and wudu/ghusl invigorates him. His statement: (Forgiven seventy pardons) means abundance, as said in similar contexts, and the meaning is that no sin remains upon him. His statement: (He said: say...) indicates that remembrance of Allah during washing is not disliked. Section: It is with tanwin (f a s l) meaning they began the prayer after finishing washing and shrouding, because the condition precedes the conditioned. His statement: (It is fard kifayah by consensus; whoever denies it becomes a disbeliever for denying consensus). The basis is the verse: 'And pray for them' (al-Tawba 9:103) and his statement: 'Pray over every righteous and sinner.' It is fard kifayah because he said: 'Pray over your companion'; if it were fard 'ayn he would not have left it. And because obliging everyone individually would cause impossibility and hardship. Congregation is not a condition. Prayer over an adult is better than over a child. It is valid to vow it because it is an intended act of worship, unlike shrouding and following the funeral. It is said it is a special characteristic of this ummah, like bequest of one-third. This is refuted by what al-Hakim authenticated that the angels prayed over Adam. So the specificity must be interpreted as merely the takbirs and manner. al-Waqidi said: It was not legislated on the day of Khadija's death, which was ten years after prophethood. And they dug a lahd for him in Mecca, and Gabriel was the imam of the angels. Ibn al-'Imad asserted it was Sheth. And they can be reconciled.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage establishes the funeral prayer as fard kifayah (communal obligation) by consensus. The primary proofs are the Quranic command 'and pray for them' and the Prophet's instruction to pray over the deceased companion. It is not fard 'ayn because the Prophet omitted it in some case. The pillars of the prayer are not detailed here but are well-known (four takbirs). The passage also clarifies that wudu is not required after carrying, washing, or embalming the deceased; Abu Hanifa holds this view. Any hadith commanding otherwise is interpreted as recommendation or precaution. The forgiveness of seventy pardons for washing is metaphorical for complete forgiveness. The supplication during washing is permissible, not disliked. Then the passage discusses the historicity of the funeral prayer, noting that it was not legislated at the time of Khadija's death (though she died after ten years of prophethood). The angels' prayer over Adam is adduced to counter the claim that it is unique to this ummah; the uniqueness is only in the specific number of takbirs or manner. The chapter heading (f a s l) with tanwin indicates a new section.

Key Terms
فرض كفاية (fard kifayah): A communal obligation; if sufficient Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved; if none do, all sin.
أركان الصلاة (arkan al-salah): The essential components of the funeral prayer; here unspecified but known as four takbirs.
لحد (lahd): A niche dug in the side of the grave, distinct from shaqq (a trench in the middle).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the funeral prayer fard kifayah and not fard 'ayn according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran
B) Because the Prophet once left it, showing it is not individual
C) Because women are exempt
D) Because it can be performed at any time

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer is a communal obligation (fard kifayah); its essential pillars are four takbirs and the final salam, and wudu after handling the deceased is not required.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Conditions for Validity of Funeral Prayer and the Dual Nature of the First Takbir
Listing and explaining the six conditions for Salat al-Janazah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for Salat al-Janazah and explain why the first takbir is both a condition and a pillar according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The first takbir in funeral prayer is both condition and pillar – a unique Hanafi position.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi outlines the six conditions for the funeral prayer and delves into a key intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the first takbir is a condition for entering prayer or a pillar substituting for a rak'ah. The author reconciles the views, affirming that it serves both functions.

Guided Path
1
List the six conditions
Identify each condition from the text: Islam of the deceased, purity, deceased in front, presence of body, standing, deceased on ground/bier.
Conditions are prerequisites; their absence invalidates the prayer.
2
Analyze the first takbir dispute
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: al-Kamal considered it only a condition; others only a pillar. Understand the evidence from al-Muhit and al-Ghayah.
The dispute hinges on whether the first takbir opens the prayer or substitutes a rak'ah.
3
Examine the proofs from al-Muhit and al-Ghayah
Al-Muhit: the prayer cannot be built on another tahrimah; al-Ghayah: the four takbirs substitute the four rak'ahs, making the first a pillar.
These texts provide the basis for the dual function.
4
Understand the reconciliation
Al-Tahtawi combines the views: the first takbir is a condition (as tahrimah) and a pillar (as rak'ah substitute). Abu Yusuf supported this dual aspect.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Apply to a scenario
If someone omits the first takbir and says only the remaining three, the prayer is invalid because both the condition and pillar are missing.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that the prayer must be repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة
التكبيرات والقيام لكن التكبيرة الأولى شرط باعتبار الشروع بها ركن باعتبار قيامها مقام ركعة كباقي التكبيرات كما في المحيط (وشرائطها) سنة أولها (إسلام الميت) لأنها شفاعة، وليست لكافر (و) الثاني (طهارته) وطهارة مكانه لأنه كالإمام (و) الثالث (تقدّمه) أمام القوم
بعض الأفاضل بأن شيئاً كان إمام البشر، جبريل إمام الملائكة، أو أن جبريل كان مبلغاً، والملائكة مقتدون به وقد يؤيد كلام ابن العماد بأن شيئاً كان لا يعلم الكيفية، فالظاهر أن الإمام جبريل ليعلم الكيفية شيث منه كا وقع للنبي في أول صلاة فرض بعد افتراض الخمس . قوله: (مع عدم الانفراد بالخطاب) فلو انفرد واحد بأن لم يحضره إلا هو تعين عليه تكفينه، ودفنه كما في الضياء، والشمني والبرهان قوله : (والقيام) فلا تصح قاعداً، أو راكباً من غير عذر كذا في الدر لأنها صلاة من وجه لوجود التحريمة، وكذا يشترط للصلاة، ولو تعذر النزول عن الدابة لطين، ونحوه ماجاز أن يصلي عليها راكباً استحساناً قوله : (لكن التكبيرة الأولى الخ) اعلم أن الكمال قال : إنّ التكبيرة الأولى شرط لأنها تكبيرة إحرام، ولذا اختصت برفع اليدين، وتعقبه في البحر والنهر بما في المحيط من أنه لا يجوز بناء صلاة جنازة على تحريمة أخرى، ولو كانت شرطاً لجاز، وذكر في الغاية أن الأربع تكبيرات قائمة مقام الأربع ركعات، وهذا يقتضي أنها ركن فجمع المصنف بينهما بهذا الجمع ويؤيد هذا الجمع ما في الكافي حيث قال : إلا أن أبا يوسف يقول في التكبيرة الأولى معنيان معنى الافتتاح، والقيام مقام ركعة، ومعنى الافتتاح يترجح فيها، ولهذا اختصت برفع اليدين ا هـ ثم في تعقب الشيخين للكمال تأمل لأنه لا يجوز بناء الفرض على تحريمه النفل أو فرض آخر مع أنها شرط لا ركن، وفي السيد نقلاً عن حاشية المؤلف أفضل صفوفها ،آخرها، وفي غيرها أولها إظهاراً للتواضع لتكون شفاعته أدعى إلى القبول ا هـ ومثله في القنية ونقله ابن ملك في شرح الوقاية عن الكرماني ا هـ قلت وينظر فيه بإطلاق ما صح في مسلم وغيره عنه خير صفوف الرجال أولها وشرها آخرها وإظهار التواضع لا يتوقف على التأخر لأن كونها أقرب إلى الإجابة إنما هو بالتحقق بالتواضع، والخضوع وذلك بالمنحة الربانية لا بالتأخر قطعاً، فيعمل بالإطلاق ما لم يوجد له مخصص صحيح، كذا بحثه بعض الأذكياء وقد علمت ما نصه أهل المذهب على أنه قد يقال : إنّ الظاهر عنوان الباطن. قوله : (أولها إسلام الميت) إما بنفسه أو بإسلام أحد أبويه، أو بتبعية الدار ، وإذا استوصف البالغ الإسلام، ولم يصفه، ومات لا يصلي كذا في شرح السيد. قوله : (لأنها شفاعة الخ) ولقوله تعالى: ﴿ولا تصل على منهم مات أبدا) [التوبة: ٩] كذا في الشرح قوله : (والثاني طهارته) عن نجاسة حكمية وحقيقية في البدن فلا تصح على من لم يغسل ولا على من عليه نجاسة، وهذا الشرط عند الإمكان فلو دفن بلا غسل ولم يمكن إخراجه إلا بالنبش سقط الغسل، وصلي على قبره بلا غسل للضرورة بخلاف ما إذا لم يهل عليه التراب بعد فإنه يخرج، ويغسل، ولو صلي عليه بلا غسل جهلاً، أو نسياناً، ثم دفن ولا يخرج إلا بالنبش أعيدت على قبره استحساناً لفساد الأولى، ويشترط طهارة الكفن إلا إذا شق ذلك لما في الخزانة أنه أن تنجس الكفن بنجاسة الميت لا يضر دفعاً للحرج بخلاف الكفن المتنجس ابتداء ا هـ. قوله: (وطهارة مكانه) قال في القنية الطهارة من النجاسة في الثوب والبدن والمكان وستر العورة شرط في حق الإمام يعني المصلي والميت جميعاً ا هـ، وفي السيد وأما مكانه أي إذا كان نجساً فإن كان الميت على الجنازة تجوز الصلاة، وإن كان على الأرض ففي الفوائد يجوزو جزم في القنية بعدمه اه؛ نهر وجه الجواز أن الكفن حائل بين الميت والنجاسة ووجه عدمه أن الكفن تابع بعد حائلاً، ثم المراد بالمكان الذي يشترط طهارته أما الجنازة، أو الأرض إن لم يكن جنازة، والحاصل أن طهارة الأرض إنما تشترط على ما في القنية إذا وضع الميت بدون جنازة أما بها فعدم اشتراط طهارة الأرض متفق عليه، ولو صلى الإمام بلا طهارة، والقوم بها أعيدت لعدم انعقاد صلاة الجميع، وبعكسه لا لسقوط الفرض بصلاة الإمام، ولو أم فيها صبي ينبغي أن لا يجوز كما في جامع أحكام الصغار بخلاف ما لو رد السلام، فإنه يسقط عن الباقين عند البعض، ولو أحدث الإمام فاستخلف غيره فيها جاز هو الصحيح، ولو افترش نعليه، وقام عليهما جاز، فلا يضر نجاسة ما تحتهما لكن لا بد من طهارة نعليه مما يلي الرجل لا مما يلي الأرض، ووقتها وقت حضورها، ولذا قدمت على سنة المغرب، ولو صلوا لغير قبله إن بتحر صحت، ولو وضعوا الرأس موضع الرجلين صحت لاستجماع شرائط الجواز، وأساؤا إن السنة المتواترة كما في البدائع. قوله : (والثالث تقدمه أمام القوم) الأولى تقديمه لأن المخاطب به الإحياء وهم فاعلوا لتقديم، فلو خلفهم لا تصح لأنه كالإمام من وجه من كل وجه بدليل صحتها على الصبي ا هـ من السيد موضحاً. قوله: (والصلاة على النجاشي) بفتح النون وكسرها واقتصر السيد في شرحه على الفتح لقب لملك الحبشة، واسمه أصحمة، ومعناه بالعربية عطية الله. قوله : (كانت بمشهده أي بمشهد النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أي بمكان راه وشاهده فيه ، فرفع له سريره حتى رآه بحضرته فتكون صلاة من خلفه على ميت يراه الإمام دون المأمومين، وهذا غير مانع من الاقتداء، أو أنها خصوصية للنجاشي، أو أن المراد بالصلاة الدعاء لا الصلاة المخصوصة ومثل ما ذكر ويقال في صلاته على زيد بن حارثة، وجعفر بن أبي طالب حين استشهد بموتة قال في البحر : وقد أثبت كلا الأولين بالدليل الكمال في الفتح، وأخرج الطبراني وابن سعد في الطبقات أن جبريل عليه السلام نزل على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بتبوك ، فقال : يا رسول الله إنّ معاوية بن معاوية مات بالمدينة أتحب أن تعمدوا التغيير لا هم من
The Book of Prayer. The takbirs and standing, but the first takbir is a condition in terms of entering the prayer, and a pillar in terms of standing in place of a rak'ah like the other takbirs, as stated in al-Muhit. (And its conditions) are six: first, (Islam of the deceased) because it is intercession, and it is not for an unbeliever. (Second: his purity and the purity of his place) because he is like the imam. (Third: his being in front) of the people...
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the six conditions for the validity of the funeral prayer (Salat al-Janazah) according to the Hanafi school. The author begins by discussing the takbirs: the first takbir has a dual nature—it is a condition for entering the prayer and also a pillar because it substitutes for a rak'ah. The conditions are: (1) the deceased must be Muslim, as the prayer is intercession and not permitted for non-Muslims (citing Quran 9:84); (2) the deceased and the place must be ritually pure, similar to the imam's requirement; (3) the deceased must be placed in front of the imam; (4) the body (or most of it including the head) must be present; (5) the person praying must not be mounted or sitting without an excuse because standing is a pillar; (6) the deceased must be placed on the ground or bier. Various details are provided, such as the case where the deceased is buried without washing, and the ruling on praying over the grave. The text also includes a discussion on the first takbir being considered both a condition and a pillar, reconciling views from Abu Yusuf and others. The incident of praying over al-Najashi is mentioned as an exception where the imam sees the deceased but the followers do not.

Key Terms
تكبيرة الأولى (takbirat al-ula): The first takbir said in Salat al-Janazah, which serves as both the opening takbir (tahrimah) and a pillar substituting for a rak'ah.
تحريمة (tahrimah): The opening takbir that prohibits worldly actions and commences the prayer.
شرائط الصلاة (shara'it al-salah): The conditions that must be fulfilled for the funeral prayer to be valid, such as Islam and purity of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi texts, what is the ruling on the first takbir in Salat al-Janazah?
A) It is only a condition (shart).
B) It is only a pillar (rukn).
C) It is both a condition and a pillar.
D) It is neither a condition nor a pillar.

Key Takeaway
The first takbir in Salat al-Janazah uniquely combines the roles of condition (tahrimah) and pillar (substitute for a rak'ah), a distinctive Hanafi position.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Conditions of Funeral Prayer (4th–6th)
Explaining three remaining conditions of salat al-janazah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for the validity of the funeral prayer in the Hanafi school (presence, standing, placement) and apply the ruling when each condition is absent, including the recognized exceptions.

Core Idea
The deceased must be present, the prayer must be standing, and the body must be on the ground — each condition has an exception and specific evidence.

We have already covered the first three conditions of salat al-janazah. Now we examine the fourth, fifth, and sixth conditions: the physical presence of the deceased, the requirement for the one praying to stand (not ride or sit without excuse), and the need for the corpse to be placed on the ground. The Hanafi school derives these from the practice of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) and the incident of al-Najashi, a miracle that confirms the general rule. This lesson walks through each condition, its proof, the allowed exceptions, and the intra- and cross-madhhab differences that arise.

Guided Path
1
List the three conditions
Identify the fourth, fifth, and sixth conditions as stated in the text: (4) presence of the deceased or most of his body, (5) the one praying must not be riding or sitting without excuse, (6) the deceased must be placed on the ground.
2
Analyze the proof for each condition
For the fourth condition, note the dalil from the story of Najashi – it was a special case (miracle) that confirms the general requirement of presence. For the fifth, standing is a rukn (pillar) of the funeral prayer. For the sixth, the deceased is considered the imam from one aspect, so he must be on the ground like the imam in regular prayer.
3
Examine the exceptions and ikhtilaf
For the fifth condition: the excused (e.g., sick) may pray sitting, but there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad holds that a standing congregation behind a sitting imam is invalid; Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa hold it valid. For the sixth condition: if the ground is muddy, the body may be placed on a bier that touches the ground. Also, the latecomer’s case is discussed.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
Based on the commentary, the chosen opinion is that these conditions are required. The intra-ikhtilaf regarding the sitting imam is resolved in favor of the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). The cross-madhhab difference with the Shafi'is on placement is noted as legitimate ikhtilaf.

كتاب الصلاة (و) الرابع (حضوره أو حضور أكثر بدنه أو نصفه مع رأسه والصلاة على النجاشي كانت بمشهده كرامة له ومعجزة للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم (و) الخامس (كون المصلي عليها غير راكب) وغير قاعد (بلا عذر لأن القيام فيها ركن فلا يترك بلا عذر (و) السادس (كون الميت) موضوعاً على الأرض لكونه الإمام من وجه فإن كان على دابة أو أبدى الناس لم تجز الصلاة على المختار إلا إن كان من عذر) كما في التبيين. قوله: (بلا عذر أما بالعذر فتصبح كما إذا كان مريضاً، ولو إماماً فصلى قاعداً، والناس خلفه قياماً أجزأه عندهما لا عند محمد بناءً على الخلاف في صحة اقتداء القائم بالقاعد، وعدمها، ولا فرق في المصلي قاعداً بعذر بين كونه ولياً، أو لا لأن كون الولي له حق التقدم لا يمنع سقوط الفرض بغيره، ولو بدون إذنه وإنما الولي له حق الإعادة، وحينئذ فلا فرق في سقوط الفرض بصلاة غير الولي بين أن يكون قائماً، أو قاعداً لعذر أفاده بعض الحذاق راداً على السيد فيما ذكره قوله : ( والسادس) كون الميت موضوعاً على الأرض) الظاهر أن اشتراط وضعه بالنسبة للمدرك الذي لم يفته شيء من التكبير خلف الإمام أما المسبوق ففي كون الوضع شرطاً له أيضاً خلاف ولهذا قالوا إذا رفعت قبل أن يقضي ما عليه من التكبير فإنه يأتي به ما لم يتباعد على قول ذكره السيد وعلى المشهور أنه يأتي به تتراً بلا دعاء إن خشي رفع الميت على الأعناق كما يأتي للمصنف . قوله : (إلا) من (عذر كأن كان بالأرض وحل لا يتأتى وضع الميت عليها . تنبيه : قال في الدور بقي من الشروط بلوغ الإمام ا هـ، وبقي منها أن يحاذي الإمام جزاً من الميت كما في القهستاني والسراج قلت : الظاهر أن هذا فيما إذا لم تكثر الموتى إذ عند كثرتها يجوز أن يجعلها صفاً واحداً ويقوم عند أفضلهم، وبقي من الشروط ستر عورته فقط، وإن كان الفرض في الكفن ستر جميع البدن لأن هذا من حيث الصلاة عليه، وذاك من حيث تكريمه وأداء حقه كذا قاله بعض الأفاضل
Book of Prayer. (And) the fourth (is his presence or presence of most of his body or half of it with his head, and the prayer over al-Najashi was in his presence as a miracle for him and a sign for the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace). (And) the fifth (is that the one praying over it is not riding) and not sitting (without excuse because standing in it is a pillar, so it is not left without excuse). (And) the sixth (is that the deceased is placed) on the ground because he is the imam from one aspect; if he is on a riding animal or the people are standing, the prayer is not valid according to the chosen opinion unless there is an excuse) as in al-Tabyin. His statement: (Without excuse, but with an excuse it is valid, as if he is sick, even if the imam prays sitting and the people behind him are standing, it suffices according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], not according to Muhammad based on the difference regarding the validity of a standing person following a sitting one, and there is no difference in the one praying sitting due to excuse whether he is a guardian or not, because the guardian having the right of precedence does not prevent the obligation falling by someone else, even without his permission; rather the guardian has the right to repeat. So then there is no difference in the falling of the obligation by the prayer of a non-guardian whether he is standing or sitting due to excuse, as some brilliant scholars have said, refuting al-Sayyid regarding what he mentioned. His statement: (And the sixth: the deceased is placed on the ground). It is apparent that the condition of placement is for the person who has not missed any takbir behind the imam; as for the latecomer, there is dispute whether placement is a condition for him as well. Hence they said: if it is lifted before he completes what he owes of takbir, he performs it as long as he has not distanced himself, according to one saying mentioned by al-Sayyid, and according to the well-known view, he performs them successively without supplication if he fears the lifting of the deceased on shoulders, as will come from the author. His statement: (Except) due to (an excuse, such as the ground being muddy such that placing the deceased on it is not feasible). Note: In al-Durr it is said: remaining among the conditions is the imam's being adult, etc. And among them is that the imam should face a part of the deceased, as in al-Qahastani and al-Siraj. I say: this applies when there are not many deceased; when they are numerous, it is permissible to make them one row and stand at the best of them. And among the conditions is covering his private parts only, even if the obligation of the shroud is to cover the whole body, because this is regarding prayer over him, and that is regarding honoring him and fulfilling his right, as some virtuous scholars said.
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage is a rapid-fire analytical refinement of the conditions (shurut) for the funeral prayer. It opens by stating the fourth condition: the presence of the deceased, meaning that the deceased must be physically present during the prayer, or at least most of his body, or half with the head. The author provides the proof from the incident of the Prophet's prayer over al-Najashi, the king of Abyssinia, which occurred while the Prophet was in Madina and the king was in Abyssinia; this was a miracle. The fifth condition requires that the person praying over the deceased must be standing and not riding or sitting without an excuse, because standing is a pillar (rukn) in this prayer. If there is an excuse, such as illness, it is permissible to pray sitting. The sixth condition requires that the deceased be placed on the ground. If the deceased is on a riding animal or the people are standing, the prayer is not valid according to the chosen opinion, unless there is an excuse such as muddy ground. The commentary then clarifies several points: the ruling regarding the latecomer who misses some takbirs, the additional conditions of the imam being an adult and facing a part of the deceased, and the condition of covering the private parts only (not the whole body) for the prayer. The hadith of Najashi is cited as a proof for the permissibility of praying over a deceased not physically present, but it is interpreted as a special miracle. The passage maintains the Hanafi position throughout, noting the ikhtilaf with Muhammad regarding a sitting imam, and confirms the mufta bihi position.

Key Terms
حضور (hudur): The physical presence of the deceased's body (or most of it) during the prayer.
مشهده (mashhaduhu): The presence of the Prophet at the time of prayer over Najashi, though the body was not present in the same location.
الصلاة على النجاشي (al-salatu 'ala al-najashi): The funeral prayer performed by the Prophet over the deceased King of Abyssinia who died in a distant land.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if the deceased is on a riding animal during the funeral prayer?
A) The prayer is valid if the people are standing.
B) The prayer is invalid on the chosen opinion.
C) The prayer is valid if the imam is also riding.
D) The prayer is valid if the deceased is an adult.

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer in the Hanafi school requires the deceased's presence, the prayer's standing, and the body on the ground — with recognized exceptions for necessity.

The First Sunnah of the Funeral Prayer: Standing at the Chest
Describing the first sunnah: imam standing by the chest of the deceased

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam’s position in the funeral prayer, explain the reason and the chosen view, and compare it with other opinions.

Core Idea
The imam stands at the deceased’s chest, as it is the seat of faith; this is sunnah, not wajib.

In the funeral prayer, the imam has a recommended position relative to the deceased. The Hanafi school emphasizes standing opposite the chest for both men and women, based on the symbolic association with the heart and faith. This lesson explores the ruling, the reasoning, and the differing opinions within and outside the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being described and what level of obligation or recommendation it carries. Here, it is the imam's position relative to the deceased in the funeral prayer, ruled as sunnah (recommended), not wajib.
Sunnah in Hanafi fiqh is a strongly recommended but non-obligatory act; omission does not require compensation.
2
Understand the reason (sabab)
The passage states that the chest is the place of the heart and the light of faith. Standing there symbolizes intercession for the deceased's faith. This reasoning supports the recommended position.
The reason is not a legal cause but a wisdom (hikmah) behind the sunnah.
3
Note the different opinions
Identify the various opinions mentioned: the chosen view (chest), a view for standing at the head for a man (seat of intellect), and a view for the middle. Also note the Shafi'i position (different for male and female).
These differences are considered legitimate ikhtilaf within and between madhabs.
4
Determine the chosen view (mufta bihi)
The passage declares that the chest position is the chosen view (al-mukhtar) and that it is the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
Tarjih is based on the authority of the narration and the reasoning provided.
5
Apply the ruling
The ruling applies equally to male and female, adult and child. If the imam stands elsewhere, the prayer is still valid (ajza'ahu), but the sunnah is missed.
This shows the distinction between sunnah and wajib; validity is maintained despite missing a sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسننها أربع الأولى (قيام الإمام بحذاء صدر الميت ذكراً كان الميت أو أنثى) لأنه موضع القلب ونور الإيمان. قال في السيد: وهو المختار، وقيل: يقوم للرجل بحذاء رأسه لأنه معدن العقل وقيل : يقوم بحذاء الوسط منهما. قوله: (ذكر) كان الميت أو أنثى فيه إشارة إلى أنه لا فرق فيما ذكر بين الصغير والكبير كما في السيد. قوله: (ونور (الأيمان بالجر أي، وموضع نور الإيمان وعبارة الشرح أولى حيث قال : لأن الصدر موضع القلب، وفيه نور الإيمان، فيكون القيام عنده إشارة إلى الشفاعة لإيمانه، وهذا ظاهر الرواية، وهو بيان الاستحباب كما سبق فلو وقف في غيره أجزأه كذا في البحر عن كافي الحاكم ا هـ، والأفضل أن تكون الصفوف ثلاثة حتى لو كانوا ستة اصطف ثلاثة، ثم
And its sunan are four: the first (is the imam's standing opposite the chest of the deceased, whether the deceased is male or female) because it is the place of the heart and the light of faith. Al-Sayyid said: It is the chosen position. And it is said: He stands for a man opposite his head because it is the mine of intellect. And it is said: He stands opposite the middle of the deceased. His statement: (male) whether the deceased is male or female, there is an indication that there is no difference in what was mentioned between a small child and an adult, as in al-Sayyid. His statement: (and the light of faith) in the genitive, i.e., and the place of the light of faith. The expression of the Sharh is better where it said: because the chest is the place of the heart, and in it is the light of faith, so standing at it is an indication of intercession for his faith. This is the apparent narration, and it is an explanation of desirability as before; if he stood elsewhere, it would suffice. Thus in al-Bahr from Kafi al-Hakim. And the best is that the rows be three, so if there are six, they line up three, then...
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage begins the enumeration of the recommended acts (sunan) of the funeral prayer. After establishing the obligatory acts (the takbirs and the taslim), the author lists the sunan, starting with the first: the imam standing opposite the chest of the deceased. This applies whether the deceased is male or female, and also whether adult or child. The reason given is that the chest contains the heart, the seat of faith, and standing there symbolizes intercession for the deceased's faith. There is a difference of opinion: some say the imam should stand at the head for a man (as the seat of intellect), and some say at the middle. However, the chosen view (as per al-Sayyid) is that he stands at the chest. The commentary clarifies that this is a sunnah (recommended), not obligatory; if the imam stands elsewhere, the prayer is still valid. The passage also notes the preference for three rows of worshippers, even if there are only six people, they should form three rows of two each. This reflects the Hanafi emphasis on order and following the sunnah in funerary rites.

Key Terms
حذاء صدر الميت (hidha' sadr al-mayyit): The position of the imam standing directly opposite the chest of the deceased.
سنن (sunan): Recommended acts (not obligatory) that complete the funeral prayer; omission does not require compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position regarding the imam's position relative to the deceased in the funeral prayer?
A) He must stand at the head for a man.
B) He stands opposite the chest for both male and female.
C) He stands at the feet for a woman.
D) He has no fixed position.

Key Takeaway
The first sunnah is for the imam to stand opposite the chest of the deceased, reflecting the seat of faith, and this applies equally to all deceased.

The Four Sunan of Janazah Prayer and the Dispute over Fatihah
Detailed listing of the four sunan and a critical discussion on Fatihah recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the four sunan of janazah prayer and explain the Hanafi ruling on reciting Fatihah, including the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The janazah prayer has four sunan; reciting Fatihah is makruh tahrimi in the Hanafi school despite the Shafi'i view.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details the four recommended acts (sunan) of the funeral prayer. While the base text suggests Fatihah may be recited as praise, the commentator rigorously refines this, showing that the relied-upon Hanafi position prohibits reciting Fatihah with the intention of Quranic recitation. Understanding this dispute is crucial for a Hanafi attending congregational funeral prayers.

Guided Path
1
List the Four Sunan
Identify each sunnah and note its position in the prayer (after which takbir it occurs).
The first sunnah concerns the imam's position; the others are verbal acts.
2
Understand the Dispute on Fatihah
Recognize that the Shafi'i school considers Fatihah fard, while the Hanafi school has a nuanced ruling.
The base text mentions permissibility, but the commentator clarifies the relied-upon view.
3
Analyze the Hadith Evidence
Examine the hadith of Ibn Abbas (in Bukhari) and the Hanafi critique of its authenticity and interpretation.
Hanafi usul: a Companion's action is not automatically marfu' (elevated to the Prophet).
4
Apply the Principle of Mura'at al-Khilaf
Learn that observing the difference (mura'at al-khilaf) is recommended only if it does not lead to a makruh in one's own madhhab.
The commentator argues that since reciting Fatihah as qira'ah is makruh tahrimi, mura'at al-khilaf does not apply.
5
Derive the Mufta Bihi
Conclude the operative ruling: recite thana (Subhanaka) after the first takbir; do not recite Fatihah with the intention of Quranic recitation.
The mufta bihi is based on books like al-Muhit, al-Tajnis, and al-Walwalijiyyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وسننها أربع الأولى (قيام الإمام بحذاء) صدر الميت ذكراً كان الميت أو أنثى) لأنه موضع القلب ونور الإيمان (و) الثانية (الثناء بعد التكبيرة الأولى) وهو سبحانك اللهم وبحمدك إلى آخره وجاز قراءة الفاتحة بقصد الثناء كذا نص عليه عندنا، وفي البخاري عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أنه صلى على جنازة فقرأ بفاتحة الكتاب، وقال: لتعلموا أنه السنة وصححه الترمذي، وقد قال أئمتنا بأن مراعاة الخلاف مستحبة، وهي فرض عند الشافعي رحمه الله فلا مانع من قصد القرآنية بها من الخلاف وحق الميت (و) الثالثة الصلاة) على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد التكبيرة (الثانية) خروجاً من الخلاف (و) الرابعة الدعاء للميت بعد التكبيرة الثالثة) قال في سكب الأنهر والأولى ترك، وجل ثناؤك إلا في صلاة الجنازة ا هـ . قوله: (وفي البخاري عن ابن عباس الخ) قال في شرح المشكاة ليس هذا من قبيل قول الصحابي من السنة كذا فيكون في حكم المرفوع كما توهمه ابن حجر ا هـ، وفي العيني على البخاري، وأجاب عنه الطحاوي بأن قراءة الفاتحة من الصحابة لعلها كانت على وجه الدعاء لا على وجه التلاوة، وقد قال مالك : قراءة الفاتحة ليس معمولاً بها في بلدنا في صلاة الجنازة ا هـ. قوله: (وقد قال أئمتنا بأن مراعاة الخلاف مستحبة الخ فيه نظر إذ ما ذكره من استحباب مراعاة الخلاف ليس على إطلاقه بل مقيد بما إذ لم يلزم عليه ارتكاب مكروه مذهبه فكان الاعتماد على ما هو مصرح به في كتب المذهب كالمحيط والتجنيس والولوالجية وغيرها من أن قراءتها بنية القراءة لا تجوز معللاً بإنها محل الدعاء دون القراءة كذا في السيد مختصراً قوله: (فلا مانع من قصد القرآنية الخ) فيه أنهم صرحوا بعدم الجواز فتكون مكروهة تحريماً، ولا يتأدى به السنة فكيف يطلب منه تلاوتها بقصد القرآنية.
(And its sunan are four: First, the imam standing opposite the chest of the deceased, whether the deceased is male or female, because it is the place of the heart and the light of faith. Second, the praise (thana) after the first takbir, which is Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika... up to its end, and it is permissible to recite al-Fatihah with the intention of praise, as it is explicitly stated in our school. In al-Bukhari, from Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) that he prayed over a funeral and recited the Fatihah, saying: 'So that you may know that it is the Sunnah.' And al-Tirmidhi authenticated it. Our imams said that observing the difference (of the Shafi'i school) is recommended, and it (recitation of Fatihah) is obligatory according to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). So there is no impediment to intending it as Quranic recitation out of consideration for the difference and the right of the deceased. Third, sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) after the second takbir, to exit from difference. Fourth, supplication for the deceased after the third takbir. He said in Sakb al-Anhur: 'And it is better to omit wa jala thana'uka except in the janazah prayer.' His saying: (In al-Bukhari from Ibn 'Abbas etc.) He said in Sharh al-Mishkat: 'This is not of the type of the Companion's saying 'it is from the Sunnah' such that it would be in the ruling of marfu' as Ibn Hajar imagined.' In al-'Ayni on al-Bukhari, al-Tahawi answered that the recitation of Fatihah by the Companions was perhaps in the manner of supplication, not recitation. And Malik said: 'Recitation of Fatihah is not practiced in our city in the janazah prayer.' His saying: (Our imams said that observing the difference is recommended) There is consideration in this, because what he mentioned about the recommendation of observing the difference is not absolute, but restricted to when it does not necessitate committing a makruh in his own madhhab. So the reliance is on what is clearly stated in the books of the madhhab, such as al-Muhit, al-Tajnis, al-Walwalijiyyah, and others, that reciting it with the intention of recitation is not permissible, with the reasoning that it is a place for supplication, not recitation. Thus in al-Sayyid, briefly. His saying: (So there is no impediment to intending it as Quranic) There is in it that they explicitly declared its impermissibility, so it would be makruh tahrimi, and the sunnah is not fulfilled by it; so how can he be asked to recite it intending Quranic recitation?
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage enumerates the four sunan (recommended acts) of the janazah prayer. The first sunnah is that the imam stands opposite the chest of the deceased, whether male or female, as the chest contains the heart, the seat of faith. Other positions (e.g., by the head for a male) are reported but the relied-upon view is the chest. The second sunnah is the recitation of thana (Subhanaka) after the first takbir. The commentator here enters a detailed discussion of whether reciting Surah al-Fatihah is permissible. The base text says it is allowed if intended as praise, not as Quranic recitation. However, the commentator refines this: while some Hanafi scholars considered it mustahabb out of khilaf (difference with Shafi'i who makes it fard), the correct view is that reciting Fatihah with the intention of Quranic recitation is not permissible (and is makruh tahrimi), because the janazah prayer is a place for dua, not Quran. The hadith of Ibn 'Abbas is explained away as either a weak proof or as the Companions doing it as dua, not recitation. The third sunnah is sending salawat on the Prophet after the second takbir, to exit from difference (with those who make it obligatory). The fourth is making dua for the deceased after the third takbir. The commentator also notes that the phrase 'wa jala thana'uka' is omitted in thana for funeral prayer.

Key Terms
الثناء (al-thanā'): The praise of Allah, specifically the supplication 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' recited after the first takbir in janazah prayer.
مراعاة الخلاف (murāʿāt al-khilāf): Observing the difference of other schools by performing an act that they consider obligatory, out of respect for their view, even if it is not obligatory in one's own school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling on reciting Surah al-Fatihah in the janazah prayer with the intention of Quran recitation?
A) It is sunnah and recommended.
B) It is permissible (mubah).
C) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
D) It is fard (obligatory).

Key Takeaway
In janazah prayer, Hanafis recite thana, not Fatihah; reciting Fatihah with Quranic intention is makruh tahrimi.

The Second, Third, and Fourth Sunan of Janazah Prayer
Completing the list of sunan with details on thana, salawat, and dua

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three sunan of janazah prayer (thana, salawat, dua) and apply the Hanafi ruling that reciting Fatihah is makruh tahrimi.

Core Idea
Thana, salawat, and dua are sunnah; reciting Fatihah is makruh tahrimi.

In this lesson, we complete the list of sunan for janazah prayer. After the first takbir comes thana (Subhanaka), after the second takbir comes salawat upon the Prophet, and after the third takbir comes dua for the deceased. We also examine the debated issue of reciting Fatihah, which the Hanafi school considers impermissible as Quranic recitation in this context.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three sunan
List the second, third, and fourth sunan: thana (after first takbir), salawat (after second takbir), and dua (after third takbir).
The first sunnah (raising hands) was covered in a previous lesson.
2
Examine the thana
After the first takbir, one recites 'Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika' omitting 'wa jala thana'uka'. Reciting Fatihah with the intention of praise is permissible according to some, but the Hanafi position is that it is makruh tahrimi if intended as Quran recitation.
The commentator stresses that observing the difference (khilaf) is not absolute; it must not lead to committing a makruh in one's own madhhab.
3
Analyze the salawat
After the second takbir, the third sunnah is to send blessings upon the Prophet. This is done to avoid the disagreement with those who consider it obligatory.
Any standard salawat formula is acceptable.
4
Analyze the dua
After the third takbir, the fourth sunnah is to make supplication for the deceased. This is the core purpose of the janazah prayer.
The right of the deceased lies in dua, not in recitation.
5
Note the fāʾida about the Prophet's funeral
The Prophet (peace be upon him) was prayed over individually without a formal imam, which is a matter of consensus. This supports the permissibility of praying janazah in congregation or individually.
This practice is an important precedent for the Hanafi ruling that an imam is not necessary for janazah prayer.

المشكاة ليس هذا من قبيل قول الصحابي من السنة كذا فيكون في حكم المرفوع كما توهمه ابن حجر ا هـ، وفي العيني على البخاري، وأجاب عنه الطحاوي بأن قراءة الفاتحة من الصحابة لعلها كانت على وجه الدعاء لا على بل مقيد بما إذ لم يلزم عليه ارتكاب مكروه مذهبه فكان الاعتماد على ما هو مصرح به في كتب المذهب كالمحيط والتجنيس والولوالجية وغيرها من أن قراءتها بنية القراءة لا تجوز معللاً بإنها محل الدعاء دون القراءة كذا في السيد مختصراً قوله: (فلا مانع من قصد القرآنية الخ) فيه أنهم صرحوا بعدم الجواز فتكون مكروهة تحريماً، ولا يتأدى به السنة فكيف يطلب منه تلاوتها بقصد القرآنية . فائدة : روي أنه لما غسل وكفن ووضع على السرير دخل أبو بكر وعمر وهما في الصف حيال رسول الله ، ومعهما نفر من المهاجرين والأنصار، بقدر ما يسع البيت، فقالا معه، حتى السلام عليك أيها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته وسلم المهاجرون والأنصار كما سلم أبو بكر وعمر، ثم قالا : اللهم إنا نشهد أنه بلغ ما أنزل إليه، ونصح لأمته، وجاهد في سبيل الله أعز الله دينه، وتمت كلمته وأومن به وحده لا شريك له، فاجعلنا الهنا ممن يتبع القول الذي وأجمع بيننا، وبينه حتى تعرفه بنا، وتعرفنا به فإنه كان بالمؤمنين رؤفاً رحيماً لا يبتغي بالإيمان بدلاً، ولا يشتري به ثمناً أبداً، والناس يقولون ،آمين، ويخرجون، ويدخل آخرون حتى صلى الرجال والنساء، ثم الصبيان، وقد قيل : إنهم الميت) قد يقال : إن حق الميت في الدعاء لا في القراءة.
After the first takbir, it is Subhanaka Allahumma wa bihamdika up to its end, and it is permissible to recite al-Fatihah with the intention of praise, as it is explicitly stated in our school. In al-Bukhari, from Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) that he prayed over a funeral and recited the Fatihah, saying: 'So that you may know that it is the Sunnah.' And al-Tirmidhi authenticated it. Our imams said that observing the difference is recommended, and it is obligatory according to al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). So there is no impediment to intending it as Quranic recitation out of consideration for the difference and the right of the deceased. (And) the third is sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) after the second takbir, to exit from difference. (And) the fourth is supplication for the deceased after the third takbir. He said in Sakb al-Anhur: 'And it is better to omit 'wa jala thana'uka' except in the janazah prayer.' His saying: (In al-Bukhari from Ibn 'Abbas etc.) He said in Sharh al-Mishkat: 'This is not of the type of the Companion's saying 'it is from the Sunnah' such that it would be in the ruling of marfu' as Ibn Hajar imagined.' In al-'Ayni on al-Bukhari, al-Tahawi answered that the recitation of Fatihah by the Companions was perhaps in the manner of supplication, not recitation. And Malik said: 'Recitation of Fatihah is not practiced in our city in the janazah prayer.' His saying: (Our imams said that observing the difference is recommended) There is consideration in this, because what he mentioned about the recommendation of observing the difference is not absolute, but restricted to when it does not necessitate committing a makruh in his own madhhab. So the reliance is on what is clearly stated in the books of the madhhab, such as al-Muhit, al-Tajnis, al-Walwalijiyyah, and others, that reciting it with the intention of recitation is not permissible, with the reasoning that it is a place for supplication, not recitation. Thus in al-Sayyid, briefly. His saying: (So there is no impediment to intending it as Quranic) There is in it that they explicitly declared its impermissibility, so it would be makruh tahrimi, and the sunnah is not fulfilled by it; so how can he be asked to recite it intending Quranic recitation? (Fāʾida): It is narrated that when he (the Prophet) was washed, shrouded, and placed on the bier, Abu Bakr and 'Umar entered, both in the row opposite the Messenger of Allah, and with them a number of the Muhajirun and Ansar, as much as the house could contain. They said with him [the greeting] until 'Peace be upon you, O Prophet, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings.' And the Muhajirun and Ansar gave salams as Abu Bakr and 'Umar had given salam. Then they said: 'O Allah, we bear witness that he has conveyed what was revealed to him, advised his ummah, and strove in the path of Allah. Allah has honored His religion and completed His word. We believe in Him alone, with no partner. So make us, O our God, among those who follow the word that is agreed upon, and gather us and him until You recognize us through him and recognize him through us. For he was to the believers kind and merciful. He does not seek a substitute for faith, nor purchase with it any price ever.' And the people said 'Amin', and they would exit, and others would enter, until the men prayed, then the women, then the children. It is said that they prayed from after noon on Monday until the same time the next day, and it is said that they remained three days praying over him. This practice, that they prayed over him individually without anyone leading them, is a matter of consensus, no disagreement therein. End quote from al-Sayyid from al-Khasa'is. His saying: (And the right of the deceased) It may be said that the right of the deceased is in supplication, not in recitation.
Source pages p. 584

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of the sunan of janazah prayer, focusing on the second, third, and fourth. The second sunnah is the thana (Subhanaka) after the first takbir. The commentator reiterates the debate about reciting Fatihah, emphasizing that the relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is not permissible (makruh tahrimi) if intended as Quran recitation. The third sunnah is sending salawat upon the Prophet after the second takbir, done to avoid the disagreement with those who consider it obligatory. The fourth is making dua for the deceased after the third takbir. The commentator also notes that in the thana for janazah, one should omit 'wa jala thana'uka'. The passage ends with a fāʾida (benefit) describing how the Prophet (peace be upon him) was prayed over individually without an imam, which is a consensus practice—this is used to support the permissibility of praying in congregation or individually, but also shows that the janazah prayer was performed without a formal imam leading. The commentator then remarks that the right of the deceased is more in supplication than recitation, reinforcing the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
الصلاة على النبي (al-ṣalātu ʿalā al-nabī): Sending blessings (e.g., 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad') upon the Prophet after the second takbir.
الدعاء للميت (al-duʿā' li al-mayyit): Supplication for the deceased after the third takbir, such as asking for forgiveness and mercy.
مراعاة الخلاف (murāʿāt al-khilāf): Observing the difference of opinion; the principle of acting in a way that avoids conflicting with another valid madhhab view, provided it does not entail a makruh in one's own madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi madhhab, after which takbir is the sunnah of sending blessings (salawat) upon the Prophet performed?
A) After the first takbir.
B) After the second takbir.
C) After the third takbir.
D) After the fourth takbir.

Key Takeaway
The second, third, and fourth sunan of janazah prayer are thana (after first takbir), salawat (after second), and dua (after third); reciting Fatihah is makruh tahrimi.

Salah — Prayer

The Fourth Sunnah: Supplication for the Deceased
Ruling and recommended supplications in janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplication in janazah prayer and distinguish between valid and invalid supplications.

Core Idea
Supplication after the third takbir is a confirmed sunnah; no specific wording is obligatory, but the transmitted du'a is best.

In the funeral prayer, after the third takbir, the imam and congregation supplicate for the deceased, themselves, and all Muslims. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position that this supplication is a sunnah mu'akkadah, not a wajib or rukn, and explains the preferred supplications based on the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that the fourth sunnah of janazah is supplication after the third takbir. Determine the hukm level: Hanafi holds it as sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed recommended), not wajib.
Sunnah mu'akkadah means the Prophet consistently did it but did not command it.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Awf ibn Malik, where the Prophet recited a specific du'a over a funeral. This shows the desirability through action.
Hadith is ahad (solitary), so thubut is zanni; therefore ruling is sunnah, not fard.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent recitation without commanding it indicates recommendation. The imperative verbs in the du'a (e.g., 'ighfir') in a prayer context indicate desirability, not obligation.
In Hanafi usul, al-amr in worship without qarinah indicates nadb.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'is consider this supplication a rukn (pillar) of janazah; some later Hanafi scholars (e.g., from Balkh) required specific wording. The relied-upon Hanafi view is that no specific wording is required.
The disagreement stems from differing weights given to the Prophet's action.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentator (al-Tahtawi) favors the transmitted du'a as 'ahsan wa ablagh' (better and more effective) but confirms the mufta bihi that any supplication for the afterlife suffices.
Tarjih is based on the principle that following the Prophet's explicit wording is superior.

O Allah, send blessings upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad until the end. (And) the fourth of the sunan is supplication for the deceased, for oneself, and for the congregation of Muslims after the third takbir. Nothing specific is prescribed for the supplication other than being for matters of the afterlife. But if one supplicates with the transmitted (supplication) from the Prophet (peace be upon him), it is better and more effective in hope of acceptance. Among it is what Awf ibn Malik memorized of the Prophet's supplication when he prayed with him over a funeral: 'O Allah, forgive him, have mercy on him, grant him well-being, pardon him, honor his lodging, widen his entrance, wash him with water, snow, and hail, purify him from sins as a white garment is cleansed from filth, and give him a house better than his house, a family better than his family...'
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof concerning the fourth sunnah of the janazah prayer. The matn states that the fourth sunnah is supplication after the third takbir for the deceased, oneself, and all Muslims. The author emphasizes that no specific wording is obligatory; rather, any supplication focusing on the afterlife suffices. However, using the transmitted supplications from the Prophet is superior due to the hope of acceptance. The commentator then expands on the transmitted supplication from Awf ibn Malik, explaining each phrase: 'forgive him' means pardon his sins, 'have mercy' means grant him compassion, 'grant him well-being' means safety from punishment, etc. The commentary includes a discussion on beginning supplication with praise of the Prophet, citing a hadith about not making him like a rider's cup. It advises starting supplication with oneself, as per Quranic examples. The commentator also clarifies that supplication is not a pillar (rukn) of the prayer. If one supplicates for worldly matters that are impossible, the prayer is not invalidated but the sunnah is not fulfilled; if possible, it invalidates. Additional transmitted supplications are provided from the Musnad of Abu Hanifa and other sources, including comprehensive formulas. The commentator notes that one may combine these or use simple phrases. The passage firmly establishes the Hanafi position that supplication is a sunnah, not wajib, and encourages following the prophetic model.

Key Terms
الدعاء للميت (al-du'a lil-mayyit): Supplication for the deceased after the third takbir of the funeral prayer.
المأثور (al-ma'thur): The transmitted supplication from the Prophet (hadith of Awf ibn Malik).
سنة (sunnah): A confirmed recommended act; omitting it does not invalidate the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The prayer is valid and the sunnah is fulfilled.
B) The prayer becomes invalid.
C) The prayer is valid but the sunnah is not fulfilled.
D) The prayer is invalid only if the deceased was a sinner.

Key Takeaway
Supplication for the deceased in janazah is a sunnah mu'akkadah; any du'a for the afterlife suffices, but the transmitted supplication is best.
