The Mandatory Salutation (Salam) in Janazah Prayer
Ruling on the final salam and its details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the salam in janazah prayer, explain the intra-madhhab disagreement on intending the deceased, and apply the proof from the practice of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
The salam in janazah prayer is wajib after the fourth takbir, not a pillar, and the imam should not raise his voice.

In the janazah prayer, the final salam is not merely a recommended act; it is obligatory (wajib) according to the Hanafi school. This lesson unpacks the ruling from the matn of Maraqi al-Falah and the commentary of al-Tahtawi, exploring the evidence, the proper method of performance, and an important inner-Hanafi dispute about whether one intends the deceased with the salam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage is regulating: the salam after the fourth takbir. Confirm that the Hanafi school classifies it as wajib (obligatory).
The text explicitly states 'yusallimu wujuban'.
2
Locate the proof
Find the source of evidence: the hadith of Ibn Umar transmitted by Imam Muhammad in his Muwatta'. Understand that this is a hadith ahad with zanni thubut, but still operative.
The hadith reads: 'Ibn Umar would pray over a janazah and then say the salam audibly to those next to him.'
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how the hadith proves the ruling. The phrase 'sallama hatta yusmi'a man yalihi' indicates the salam is performed audibly, and from the practice of a sahabi, the Hanafi school derives the obligation.
Imam Muhammad says 'bihadha na'khudh' (this is what we adopt).
4
Unpack the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Consider the disagreement about intention: should one intend the deceased with the salam? The stronger view (al-Bahr) says no, because the deceased is not addressed. Some later scholars allow it as supplication.
The mufta bihi is not to intend the deceased.
5
Determine the practical application
Apply the rulings: the imam performs two salams (right and left), does not raise his voice excessively, and the salam is heard only by those next to him.
The loudness is moderate, unlike regular prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويسلم وجوباً بعد التكبيرة الرابعة من غير دعاء بعدها في ظاهر الرواية واستحسن بعض المشايخ أن يقول : ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة الخ، أو ربنا لا تزغ قلوبنا الخ، وينوي بالتسليمتين الميت مع القوم كما ينوي الإمام ولا ينبغي أن يرفع صوته بالتسليم فيها كما يرفع في سائر الصلوات ويخافت بالدعاء، ويجهر بالتكبير قوله : (وينوي بالتسليمتين الميت مع القوم وجزم في الظهيرية بأنه لا ينوي الميت، ومثله لقاضيخان وفي الجوهرة قال في البحر : وهو الظاهر لأن الميت لا يخاطب بالسلام لأنه ليس أهلاً للخطاب قال بعض الفضلاء، وفيه نظر لأنه ورد أنه كان يسلم على أهل القبور ا هـ على أن المقصود منه الدعاء لا الخطاب قوله : (ولا ينبغي أن يرفع صوته بالتسليم فيها قال الزيلعي ويخافت في الكل إلا في التكبير ومشايخ بلخ قالوا: السنة أن يسمع كل صف الصف الذي بعده، وعن أبي يوسف أنه لا يجهر كل الجهر، ولا يسر كل الأسرا رحموي عن الظهيرية كذا في السيد، وروى الإمام محمد في موطئه عن مالك حدثنا نافع أن ابن عمر كان إذا صلى على جنازة سلم حتى يسمع من يليه قال محمد: وبهذا نأخذ فيسلم عن يمينه، ويساره ويسمع من يليه وهو قول أبي حنيفة
And he says the salutation wajib after the fourth takbir without supplication after it in the apparent narration. Some mashayikh recommended saying: 'Our Lord, give us in this world good...' or 'Our Lord, do not let our hearts deviate...' And he intends by the two salutations the deceased along with the people, as the imam intends. He should not raise his voice in the salutation therein as he raises it in other prayers; he should lower his voice in supplication and raise it in takbir. His statement: 'And he intends by the two salutations the deceased along with the people.' It is firmly stated in al-Zahiriyyah that he does not intend the deceased, and similarly for Qadikhan and in al-Jawharah. Al-Bahr says: 'It is apparent, because the deceased is not addressed with salutation as he is not fit for address.' Some virtuous ones said: 'This is questionable because it is reported that he used to greet the people of the graves.' But it is understood that the intention is supplication, not address.
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the salam in the janazah prayer. The matn states that the salam after the fourth takbir is wajib (obligatory), not merely sunnah, according to the zahir al-riwayah. The commentator then discusses the intention: should one intend the deceased along with the congregation when making salam? There is an ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school. The stronger view cited from al-Bahr is that one does not intend the deceased because salutation is an address, and the deceased is not capable of receiving address. However, some scholars note that the Prophet used to greet the dead, so it may be permissible as a supplication, not literal address. The commentator also discusses the loudness of the salam: it should not be raised like in other prayers; the imam should make it audible only to those next to him. This is based on the practice of Ibn Umar and the view of Abu Hanifa. The commentator provides a detailed discussion of differing views among Hanafi scholars, concluding with the relied-upon position that the imam says salam to his right and left, making it audible to those next to him. The underlying principle is that the janazah prayer is not a full prayer with ruku' and sujud, so its rulings have unique features.

Key Terms
التسليم (al-taslim): The final salutation ending the janazah prayer.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted ruling from the Hanafi authorities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is sunnah.
B) It is wajib after the fourth takbir.
C) It is optional.
D) It is fard kifayah.

Key Takeaway
The salam in janazah prayer is wajib, performed twice audibly to those nearby, and the preferred view is not to intend the deceased.

Raising Hands in Janazah Takbirs: The Hanafi Position and Its Proof
Dispute on raising hands during takbirs of funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during janazah takbirs, cite the primary hadith evidence, and distinguish the relied-upon view from the analogy-based objection.

Core Idea
In janazah, hands are raised only in the first takbir — the Prophet did not repeat the gesture.

You are standing in a funeral prayer. As the imam says 'Allahu Akbar' for the first time, you raise your hands to your ears. But when the second, third, and fourth takbirs come, you wonder: should you raise your hands again? This lesson resolves that question by examining the primary textual evidence and the competing analogy. We will see why the Hanafi school holds that only the first takbir includes raising hands, and why this view is preferred over the opinion of some later Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Raf' al-yadayn (raising hands) in the janazah prayer is a sunnah act. The dispute is whether it applies to all takbirs or only the first.
2
State the zahir al-riwayah position
According to the apparent narration of Imam Muhammad, hands are raised only in the first takbir, not in subsequent ones.
This is the primary transmitted view.
3
Present the dissenting view of Mashayikh Balkh
Many scholars of Balkh analogized janazah takbirs to the takbirs of regular prayer, arguing that hands should be raised in every takbir.
Their basis: each takbir is like a rak'ah.
4
Examine the dalil
Al-Daraqutni narrates that the Prophet raised his hands only in the first takbir 'then did not return' (thumma la ya'ud). This hadith explicitly limits the act.
Hadith is ahad but considered sound for practice.
5
Understand the tarjih
The commentator (al-Tahtawi) affirms that the zahir al-riwayah is al-sahih (the correct view), as stated in al-Mabsut, because the hadith is explicit and janazah prayer is fundamentally different from regular prayer.
The mufta bihi is to raise hands only at the first takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يرفع يديه في غير التكبيرة الأولى في ظاهر الرواية وكثير من مشايخ بلخ اختاروا الرفع في كل تكبيرة كما كان قوله: (في ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح نهر عن المبسوط لما روى الدارقطني عن ابن عباس وأبي هريرة أن النبي كان إذا صلى على جنازة رفع يديه في أول تكبيرة، ثم لا يعود ولأن كل تكبيرة قائمة مقام ركعة وغير الركعة الأولى لا رفع فيها فكذا تكبيرات الجنازة، وقالوا: يفسدها ما يفسد الصلاة، وتكره في الأوقات المكروهة، فلو صلوا فيها اهـ.
And he does not raise his hands in other than the first takbir in the apparent narration. Many mashayikh of Balkh chose raising in every takbir just as (he would) in other prayers. His statement: 'In the apparent narration, and it is the correct view as in al-Mabsut, because al-Daraqutni narrated from Ibn Abbas and Abu Hurairah that the Prophet, when he prayed over a funeral, raised his hands in the first takbir and then did not return. And because every takbir stands in place of a rak'ah, and there is no raising in other than the first rak'ah, so likewise the takbirs of the funeral. And they said: Whatever invalidates the prayer invalidates it, and it is disliked in disliked times. So if they prayed in them... (end).
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding raising the hands during the takbirs of the janazah prayer. The matn states the position of the zahir al-riwayah: hands are raised only in the first takbir, not in the subsequent ones. The commentator then explains that many scholars from Balkh chose to raise hands in every takbir, by analogy to other prayers. The proof for the first position is a hadith from al-Daraqutni that the Prophet raised his hands only in the first takbir. Additionally, since each takbir in janazah is analogous to a rak'ah in regular prayer, and in regular prayer hands are raised only in the first rak'ah (according to the Hanafi view), the same applies here. The commentator concludes that the zahir al-riwayah position is the correct one (al-sahih), as found in al-Mabsut. The dispute shows diversity within the Hanafi school, with some later scholars (e.g., from Balkh) preferring the analogy to other prayers over the hadith evidence. The relied-upon position for fatwa is the zahir al-riwayah: only the first takbir includes raising hands.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising hands to the ears during the takbirat al-ihram and other takbirs.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted ruling from the six books of Imam Muhammad, considered the primary authority.
مشايخ بلخ (Mashayikh Balkh): Scholars from the region of Balkh in Central Asia, known for their preference for qiyas in this issue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Hands are raised in all four takbirs.
B) Hands are raised only in the first takbir.
C) Hands are not raised at all.
D) It is optional.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet raised his hands only in the first takbir of janazah; this is the operative ruling in the Hanafi school.

Rulings on Salam, Raising Hands, and Supplication in Funeral Prayer
Commentary on multiple rulings of salat al-janazah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on salam, hand-raising, and supplication in the funeral prayer and identify the relied-upon positions in the face of intra-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
In the funeral prayer, hands are raised only at the first takbir, and the salam is said without follow-up supplication — these are the Zahir al-Riwayah positions.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya clarifies several disputed rulings in the funeral prayer. While the death prayer is simple in structure, subtle differences exist within the Hanafi school, particularly regarding hand-raising and the format of the salam. The author distinguishes between the relied-upon narrations (Zahir al-Riwayah) and preferred views of later scholars, guiding the mufti to the soundest practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage addresses multiple elements: salam (wajib after fourth takbir), hand-raising (only at first takbir in Zahir al-Riwayah), following the imam in extra takbirs, and supplication for non-mukallaf deceased.
Each element has a specific ruling and evidence.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
The salam supplication is based on the hadith of Awf ibn Malik (Muslim etc.). Hand-raising ruling is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Abu Huraira (Darqutni). The prohibition of istighfar for children/insane is based on lack of sin.
The dalil for the hand-raising rule is weak in transmission (zanni al-thubut) but accepted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith of Awf provides the exact supplication text. The hand-raising hadith shows the Prophet only raised hands once, indicating the normative practice.
The imperative in the hadith is interpreted as recommendation, not obligation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The Balkh school preferred raising hands in every takbir, citing Ibn Umar's practice. This conflicts with the Zahir al-Riwayah position.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate but the tarjih favors the prophetic practice.
5
Evaluate the tarjih and identify the mufta bihi
Al-Tahtawi states the relied-upon position is the Zahir al-Riwayah: no hand-raising after the first takbir. The fifth takbir is not followed, and the follower waits for the imam's salam.
The authority_weight is zahir_riwayah, which is the core layer of Hanafi transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وزوجاً خيراً من زوجه وأدخله الجنة وأعذه من عذاب القبر وعذاب النار) قال عوف رضي الله عنه : حتى تمنيت أن أكون أنا ذلك الميت رواه مسلم والترمذي والنسائي، وفي الأصل روايات أخر (ويسلم) وجوباً (بعد) التكبيرة الرابعة) من غير دعاء) بعدها (في ظاهر الرواية) واستحسن بعض المشايخ أن يقول : ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة الخ، أو ربنا لا تزغ قلوبنا الخ، وينوي بالتسليمتين الميت مع القوم كما ينوي الإمام ولا ينبغي أن يرفع صوته بالتسليم فيها كما يرفع في سائر الصلوات ويخافت بالدعاء، ويجهر بالتكبير (ولا يرفع يديه في غير التكبيرة الأولى في ظاهر الرواية وكثير من مشايخ بلخ اختاروا الرفع في كل تكبيرة كما كان يفعله ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما (ولو) كبر الإمام خمساً لم يتبع) لأنه منسوخ (ولكن ينتظر سلامه في المختار) ليسلم معه في الأصح وفي رواية يسلم المأموم كما كبر إمامه الزائدة ولو سلم الإمام بعد الثلاثة ناسياً كبر الرابعة ويسلم ولا يستغفر لمجنون وصبي) إذ لا ذنب لهما (ويقول) في الدعاء (اللهم اجعله فرطاً) الفرط بفتحتين الذي يتقدم الإنسان من ولده أي أجراً
And a spouse better than his spouse and enter him into Paradise and protect him from the punishment of the grave and the punishment of the Fire. Awf (may Allah be pleased with him) said: Until I wished that I were that deceased person. Narrated by Muslim, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i. In the original there are other narrations. (And he says salam) as an obligation (after) the fourth takbir (without any supplication) after it (in the apparent narration). Some mashayikh considered it good to say: 'Our Lord, give us in this world good...' or 'Our Lord, do not deviate our hearts...'. And he intends with both salams the deceased along with the people, just as the imam intends. It is not appropriate for him to raise his voice in salam therein as he does in other prayers. He lowers his voice in supplication and raises it in takbir. (And he does not raise his hands in other than the first takbir in the apparent narration, and many mashayikh of Balkh chose raising in every takbir as Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) used to do. (And if) the imam says a fifth takbir, he does not follow) because it is abrogated. (But he waits for his salam in the chosen view) to say salam with him in the most correct view. In one narration, the follower says salam as soon as his imam says the additional one. And if the imam after three forgetfully says salam, he says the fourth takbir and says salam. (And he does not seek forgiveness for the insane and the child) because they have no sin. (And he says) in the supplication: (O Allah, make him a 'farat') – 'farat' with two fathas means one who precedes from his child, i.e., a reward.
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya of al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah covers several key rulings of the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah). It opens with a supplication narrated in the hadith of Awf ibn Malik, which includes asking for a good spouse, entry into paradise, and protection from punishment. Then it addresses the salam: according to Zahir al-Riwayah, the salam is obligatory after the fourth takbir with no supplication following it, though some scholars recommend a brief dua like 'Rabbana atina' or 'Rabbana la tuzigh'. The person praying makes the intention for both the deceased and the congregation (if imam). The Imam should not raise his voice in salam but should in takbir, and should lower his voice in supplication. On raising hands, the Zahir al-Riwayah position is that hands are only raised in the first takbir, but the Balkh school preferred raising in every takbir, citing Ibn Umar's practice. However, the Hanafi relied-upon position is the first. If the imam adds a fifth takbir, it is not followed because it is abrogated; the follower waits for the imam's salam. If the imam forgetfully says salam after three takbirs, he must do a fourth and then salam. Regarding the deceased, we do not seek forgiveness for an insane person or a young child because they had no moral responsibility. The supplication 'Allahummaj'alhu faratan' means make him a preceding reward for us.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The transmitted narrations from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani that form the foundation of the Hanafi school, considered the most authoritative layer of transmission.
فرط (farat): A child who precedes his parents to the afterlife, considered a reward and intercessor for them.
لا يستغفر (la yastaghfir): One does not ask forgiveness for the deceased if they are an insane person or a child who died before puberty, as they have no sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view in Zahir al-Riwayah, when does the imam raise his hands in the funeral prayer?
A) At every takbir
B) Only at the first takbir
C) At the first and fourth takbir
D) No hand raising at all

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi funeral prayer, the salam follows the fourth takbir without added supplication, hands are raised only at the first takbir, and seeking forgiveness is not done for children or the insane.

Following Imam in Extra Takbirs in Janazah
Ruling on the follower's action when imam says extra takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower's action when the imam says extra takbirs in janazah prayer and apply the proof from consensus.

Core Idea
An abrogated act is not followed; the follower waits for the imam's salam.

This lesson examines the ruling when an imam in janazah prayer says more than four takbirs. Although the follower is generally required to follow the imam, this rule has limits when the act is abrogated. The correct approach according to the preferred Hanafi view is to wait for the imam's salam. We will explore the evidence from the consensus of the Companions and the difference of narration within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam saying a fifth takbir. The ruling is that the follower does not follow the imam in this extra takbir.
The act is specific to the follower's response.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the consensus of the Companions that the final practice of the Prophet was four takbirs, and that extra takbirs are abrogated.
The text states: 'because the takbirs are four, the last action of the Prophet, and the consensus settled upon it'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'the last action of the Prophet and the consensus settled upon it' indicates that the established sunnah is four takbirs; any addition is not part of the sunnah and thus abrogated.
Abrogated acts are not to be followed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an intra-Hanafi narration that the follower says salam with the imam's additional takbir. However, the preferred view is to wait for the imam's salam.
The difference is within the Hanafi school.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The preferred view is chosen because following in an abrogated act is wrong; waiting for salam is not a mistake as the sanctity of prayer remains until salam.
Al-Marghinani and others prefer waiting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يفعله ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما (ولو) كبر الإمام خمساً لم يتبع) لأنه منسوخ (ولكن ينتظر سلامه في المختار) ليسلم معه في الأصح وفي رواية يسلم المأموم كما كبر إمامه الزائدة ولو سلم الإمام بعد الثلاثة ناسياً كبر الرابعة ويسلم ولا يستغفر لمجنون وصبي) إذ لا ذنب لهما (ويقول) في الدعاء (اللهم اجعله فرطاً) الفرط بفتحتين الذي يتقدم الإنسان من ولده أي أجراً ارتكبوا النهي ولا إعادة عليهم كما في الفتح والبحر وتكره وقت الخطبة كما في المضمرات، ويكره تأخيرها إلى ذلك الوقت ليجتمع عليها الناس كذا في ابن أمير حاج. قوله: (كما كان يفعله ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما الرواية عنه مضطربة فإنه روي عنه وعن علي أنهما قالا لا يرفع إلا عند تكبيرة الافتتاح ولئن صحت فلا تعارض فعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كما في الفتح، والتبيين والحلبي والشمني. قوله : ( لأنه منسوخ ولا متابعة في المنسوخ كقنوت الفجر لأنّ التكبير أربعاً آخر فعله واستقر عليه إجماع الصحابة قوله : (ولكن ينتظر سلامه في المختار) لأن البقاء في حرمة الصلاة بعد الفراغ منها ليس بخطأ إنما الخطأ في المتابعة نهر بخلاف العيد إذا زاد على ثلاث تكبيرات فإنه لأنه يتبع مجتهد فيه، ولو جاوز حد الاجتهاد لا يتابع والخلاف فيما إذا سمع التكبير من الإمام فلو من المبلغ تابعه إجماعاً حموي، وينوي الافتتاح بكل تكبيرة تزيد على الأربع كما في العيد نهر لاحتمال شروعه قبل الإمام ا هـ من السيد ملخصاً. قوله : (كما كبر) استعمل الكاف في المفاجأة أي يكبر إذا انتقل إمامه إلى الزائدة وبالأول يفتى. قوله : (كبر) أي الإمام الرابعة، ويسلم ولم يبينوا هل يجب عليه سجود السهو، ويحتمل أن الضمير راجع إلى المأموم، وهو بعيد لأنّ الإمام إذا اقتصر على ثلاثة فسدت فيما يظهر، وإذا فسدت على الإمام فسدت على المأموم لترك ركن من أركانها
Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) used to do it. (And if) the imam says five takbirs, he is not followed because it is abrogated. But in the preferred view, he waits for his salam so that he may say salam with him. In the soundest narration, the follower says salam as his imam says the additional takbir. If the imam says salam after three [takbirs] forgetfully, he says the fourth takbir and says salam, and he does not seek forgiveness for an insane person or a child, for they have no sin. And he says in the supplication: 'O Allah, make him a predecessor (farat)...' The farat (with two fathas) is the one who precedes a person from among his children, i.e., reward. They committed the prohibition and there is no repetition upon them, as in al-Fath and al-Bahr. It is disliked at the time of the sermon, as in al-Mudmarat. It is disliked to delay it to that time so that people gather for it, as in Ibn Amir Hajj. His statement: (as Ibn Umar used to do it) — the narration from him is contradictory, for it is narrated from him and from Ali that they both said: do not raise [the hands] except at the opening takbir. Even if it is authentic, it does not oppose the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him), as in al-Fath, al-Tabyin, al-Halabi, and al-Shumni. His statement: (because it is abrogated and there is no following in the abrogated, like the qunut of Fajr, because the takbirs are four, the last action of the Prophet, and the consensus of the Companions settled upon it). His statement: (but he waits for his salam in the preferred view) because remaining in the sanctity of prayer after finishing it is not wrong; the wrong is in following. In al-Nahr, unlike Eid when he adds to three takbirs, he is followed because it is a matter of ijtihad. If he exceeds the limit of ijtihad, he is not followed. The difference is when he hears the takbir from the imam; if it is from the announcer, he follows him by consensus, as in al-Hamawi. He intends the opening takbir with every additional takbir beyond four, as in Eid, in al-Nahr, due to the possibility of his starting before the imam, summarized from al-Sayyid. His statement: (as he said takbir) — the kaf is used for suddenness, i.e., he says takbir when his imam moves to the additional one, and the first is the fatwa. His statement: (he said takbir) means the imam says the fourth takbir and says salam, and they did not clarify whether sajdah al-sahw is required. It is possible that the pronoun refers to the follower, but it is far-fetched because if the imam limits to three, the prayer is invalid apparently, and if it is invalid for the imam, it is invalid for the follower due to omitting a pillar.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This is a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi's hashiya on the ruling of extra takbirs in janazah prayer. The matn states that if the imam says five takbirs, the follower should not follow him because the fifth takbir is abrogated; the established sunnah is four takbirs. The preferred view (mukhtar) is that the follower waits for the imam's salam and then says salam with him. However, there is a narration that the follower says salam when the imam says the extra takbir. The commentator explains the proofs: the action of Ibn Umar is not authoritative against the Prophet's practice; the abrogation is established by the consensus of the Companions that the final practice was four takbirs. The follower should not follow in an abrogated act, like the qunut of Fajr. Waiting for the imam's salam is not a mistake because the sanctity of prayer remains until salam. In Eid prayer, if the imam adds a takbir beyond the three (in the second rak'ah for some views), he is followed because it is a matter of ijtihad, but if he exceeds the limit of ijtihad, he is not followed. If the follower hears the takbir from the imam directly, he follows; if from a transmitter, he follows by consensus. Each additional takbir beyond four should be intended as the opening takbir, similar to Eid, due to the possibility that the follower might have started after the imam. The commentator also discusses the case where the imam forgetfully says salam after three takbirs and then realizes the mistake; he should say a fourth takbir and then salam. The scholars did not clarify whether sajdah al-sahw is required, and it is unlikely that the pronoun in 'walam yubayyinu' refers to the follower, because if the imam limits to three takbirs, the prayer is invalid, and if invalid for the imam, it is also invalid for the follower.

Key Terms
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; the ruling that was valid earlier is replaced by a later one.
مختار (mukhtar): The preferred opinion among the Hanafi scholars for practice and fatwa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an imam in janazah prayer says five takbirs, what should the follower do according to the preferred Hanafi view?
A) Say a fifth takbir and follow the imam.
B) Wait for the imam's salam and then say salam with him.
C) Leave the prayer immediately.
D) Complete four takbirs and then say salam without waiting.

Key Takeaway
In janazah prayer, the follower does not follow the imam in extra takbirs beyond four; he waits for the imam's salam because the extra takbirs are abrogated.

Distinguishing Congenital vs. Acquired Insanity in Janazah Istighfar
Ruling that istighfar is not said for children and the insane in janazah, with a refinement distinguishing congenital from acquired insanity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between congenital and acquired insanity in the ruling of istighfar in janazah prayer and explain the basis for the Hanafi distinction.

Core Idea
Istighfar is omitted for those never obligated, but permitted for those who sinned before losing sanity.

The classic Hanafi text states that one does not seek forgiveness for an insane person or a child in the janazah prayer. However, later jurists refined this ruling by distinguishing between congenital insanity and insanity that occurs after the age of accountability. This lesson unpacks that refinement, focusing on the underlying rationale of taklif (legal obligation) and sin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Base Ruling
Read the matn statement: 'لا يستغفر لمجنون وصبي' — one does not seek forgiveness for an insane person or a child. Understand the general application.
The matn treats both equally without qualification.
2
Examine the Refinement by al-Burhan al-Halabi
Al-Burhan al-Halabi restricts the ruling to congenital insanity (الأصلي) because such a person was never a mukallaf. For one who becomes insane after taklif (العارض), the obligation was present before insanity, so istighfar is permissible.
The key term is 'العرض' meaning acquired or intermittent.
3
Understand the Rationale
The sharh's reasoning 'إذ لا ذنب لهما' (for they have no sin) applies only to those who never had sin. The congenital insane and child have no sin, but the one who became insane later may have sins from before.
This reinforces the distinction based on the presence or absence of previous obligation.
4
Apply the Distinction
In practice, when performing janazah for an insane person, determine whether the insanity is congenital or acquired. If congenital, omit istighfar; if acquired, include it.
This nuance is accepted in later Hanafi fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ولا يستغفر (لمجنون) قال البرهان الحلبي : ينبغي أن يقيد بالأصلي لأنه لم يكلف بخلاف العارض فإنه قد كلف، وعروض الجنون ما قبله، بل هو كسائر الأمراض ا هـ ويدل عليه تعليل الشرح بقوله إذ لا ذنب لهما
His statement: 'and he does not seek forgiveness for an insane person' — al-Burhan al-Halabi said: It should be restricted to the congenital [insane person] because he is not obligated, unlike the one who becomes insane later, for he was obligated before his insanity. The onset of insanity does not remove the past obligation; rather, it is like other illnesses. This is supported by the reasoning of the sharh when it says 'for they have no sin.'
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This is a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi's hashiya clarifying the ruling on seeking forgiveness (istighfar) in janazah prayer for an insane person or a child. The matn states that one does not seek forgiveness for them. Al-Tahtawi quotes al-Burhan al-Halabi who restricts this ruling to the congenital insane person, i.e., one who was born insane or has been insane since before the age of accountability (taklif). The reason is that such a person never became obligated (mukallaf), so they have no sins to be forgiven. In contrast, a person who becomes insane after reaching the age of accountability (al-'arid) was previously obligated and may have sins; therefore, seeking forgiveness for them is allowed. The 'arud (onset) of insanity does not erase past obligations, similar to how physical illness does not. This distinction is supported by the sharh's reasoning that the child and insane have no sin: this applies only to the one who never was obligated, not to the one who was obligated but later lost sanity.

Key Terms
العرض (al-'arud): That which appears later, i.e., acquired insanity as opposed to congenital.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the refined Hanafi position in this lesson, for which of the following should one NOT seek forgiveness in the janazah du'a?
A) A man who became insane after age 20.
B) A woman born with severe intellectual disability.
C) A child who died at age 7.
D) Both B and C.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on istighfar in janazah turns on whether the deceased ever became mukallaf, not merely on the presence of insanity.

The Recommended Supplication for a Deceased Child in Janazah
Critical refinement of the supplication for a child's janazah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended du'a for a deceased child in the Hanafi school and explain the preferred interpretation of the term 'farat'.

Core Idea
The Hanafi du'a for a deceased child asks Allah to make the child a predecessor, a treasure, and an intercessor for the parents.

In the janazah prayer for a child, the Hanafi school prescribes a specific supplication that goes beyond simple forgiveness. This lesson explores the wording and meaning of that du'a, as critically refined by later Hanafi commentators like al-Tahtawi. Understanding this du'a deepens one's appreciation of the child's spiritual benefit for the parents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of the du'a
The recommended supplication comprises asking for the child to be a farat, a reward (ajr), a treasure (dhukhr), and an intercessor (shafi' mushaffa').
The du'a is recited after the fourth takbir.
2
Analyze the term 'farat'
Al-Tahtawi prefers interpreting 'farat' as 'a predecessor who prepares benefits in Paradise' rather than 'reward' to avoid repetition with the word 'ajr'.
The repetition would occur in the phrase 'wa aj'alhu lana ajran'.
3
Understand the scope of the du'a
The child as a farat is primarily for his parents and their like, not all worshippers, because the right of precedence belongs to the parents.
This is a criticism of the view that the du'a applies to every worshipper.
4
Note additional elements
The du'a also includes asking for the child to be a treasure (dhukhr) and an intercessor (shafi' mushaffa'), plus supplication for the parents.
The hadith from al-Mughirah mentions praying for the parents of a miscarriage.
5
Connect to practice
This du'a is recited after the fourth takbir, with recommended raising of hands at chest level.
Raising hands is a sunnah practice in janazah du'a.

أي) ثواباً) أفاد أنّ الأجر والثواب مترادفان، وقيل: الثواب هو الحاصل بأصول الشرع، والأجر هو الحاصل بالمكملات لأنّ الثواب لغة بدل العين والأجر بدل المنفعة وهي تابعة للعين ولا ينكر إطلاق أحدهما على الآخر. قوله : (الذخيرة) هي أعد لوقت الحاجة، وهو معنى قولهم في تفسيرها خيراً .باقياً قوله : (واجعله لنا شافعاً) اسم فاعل من شفع الثلاثي، وهو الذي يشفع لغيره. قوله : (مشفعاً) بتشديد الفاء المفتوحة اسم مفعول من شفع المضعف العين. قوله : (مقبول الشفاعة وفي العيني هو الذي يجعل شفيعاً، ولا شك أن إذنه تعالى بالشفاعة يستلزم قبولها، وفي المفيد يدعو لوالديه أي والدي الصغير، وقيل: يقول: اللهم ثقل به المبتغى بالمعجمة، ويستحب أن يرفع يديه عند الدعاء بحذاء ،صره، ثم يكبر رابعة | هـ ، وفي تخريج الهداية روى أصحاب السنن عن المغيرة قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : السقط يصلى عليه، ويدعى لوالديه بالمغفرة، وفي رواية بالعافية والرحمة الحديث وصححه الترمذي، والحاكم وقالوا أن الألم بالغم والهم والحسرة والوحشة والضغطة تعم الأطفال، وغيرهم، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
His statement: 'and he says in the supplication, etc.' — i.e., after completing his statement 'and whoever among us You take, then take him in faith' as in al-Halabi, al-Tanwir, and others. His statement: 'i.e., an advanced reward' — he followed Miskeen, al-Ayni and others in this, but al-Bahr rejected it due to repetition in the phrase 'and make him for us a reward'. Rather, as in al-Siraj, one should say 'a predecessor preparing our benefits in Paradise'. This is also a supplication for the boy for his advancement in goodness, especially since they said the good deeds of the child are for him, not for his parents; rather, the parents have the reward of teaching. I say: preparing benefits in Paradise is part of the advanced reward, and repetition does not harm because the context requires it, as similarly occurred in the supplication of Awf ibn Malik. Then, making the child a 'farat' for all the worshippers is not apparent, because he is only a farat for his parents and their like. Similarly, saying he is a reward. It was responded that this is required from the parent because his right to precedence is his; but it was rebutted that this supplication is required from every worshipper, and the parent may be ignorant and not precede, or dead, given that the rank of parents is delayed. 'Advanced and make him for us a reward' i.e., reward; 'and a treasure' (dhukhra) with a dammah on the dhal and sukun on the kha: the treasure; 'and make him for us an intercessor whose intercession is accepted' with a fatha on the fa: accepted intercession. Regarding other governors, it may be said that the worshipper, through his effort, prayer, and condolence, has reward written for him. So making the child a reward, i.e., a cause of reward, is apparent for every worshipper. If 'farat' means reward, the matter is clear. If 'farat' means the one who precedes and prepares benefits without the restriction of parents, it is also apparent. His statement: 'i.e., reward' indicates that ajr and thawab are synonymous. It is said that thawab is what is obtained through the fundamentals of the Shariah, while ajr is what is obtained through completions, because thawab linguistically is the substitute for the substance, and ajr is the substitute for the benefit, which is subordinate to the substance, and one does not deny the application of one for the other. His statement: 'the treasure' (al-dhukhra) is what is prepared for times of need. His statement: 'and make him for us a shafi'' (intercessor) is an active participle from shafa'a (to intercede). His statement: 'mushaffa'an' (accepted intercession) is a passive participle from the doubled verb. In al-Ayni, he is the one who is made an intercessor, and there is no doubt that Allah's permission for intercession entails its acceptance. In al-Mufeed, he supplicates for his parents, i.e., the parents of the child. It is said: say 'O Allah, make heavy thereby their scales, and increase their rewards. O Allah, place him in the care of Ibrahim, and join him with the righteous believers.' Al-Bahr said: I have not seen anyone state clearly that one should make supplication for the master of the deceased slave, but it should be done for him as for the deceased. In Ibn Amir Hajj, from al-Mubtagha (with a mu'jama), and it is recommended to raise hands while supplicating in line with his chest, then say the fourth takbir. In Takhrij al-Hidayah, the authors of Sunan narrated from al-Mughirah that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The miscarriage (saqt) is prayed over, and supplication is made for its parents for forgiveness.' In another narration: 'for well-being and mercy.' The hadith was authenticated by al-Tirmidhi and al-Hakim. They said that pain due to grief, worry, regret, loneliness, and distress affects children and others. And Allah knows best. I seek forgiveness from Allah the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This is a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi's hashiya explaining the recommended supplication (du'a) for a deceased child in the janazah prayer. The matn says to say: 'O Allah, make him a farat (predecessor) i.e., reward.' The commentator discusses different interpretations: 'farat' means a reward that precedes, or one who prepares benefits in Paradise. He rejects the view that it means a reward (ajr) because it would cause repetition with 'make him for us a reward'. He prefers the interpretation of 'a predecessor preparing our benefits in Paradise'. The du'a is also for the child's advancement in goodness, and the child's own good deeds are for him, not for his parents, but parents get reward for teaching. The commentator also discusses whether the child can be a 'farat' for all worshippers; he says only for parents. The supplication also includes asking for treasure (dhukhra) and intercession (shafa'ah). He explains the meanings of shafi' and mushaffa'. He also mentions that the supplication should include praying for the child's parents: asking forgiveness for them, etc. He cites a hadith from al-Mughirah about praying for the parents of a miscarriage. He also notes that it is recommended to raise hands during the du'a, at chest level, then say the fourth takbir. This du'a is part of the sunnah of janazah prayer for a child.

Key Terms
فرط (farat): A predecessor who prepares benefits for others, especially a child who precedes his parents to Paradise.
ذخر (dhukhr): A treasure stored for the Hereafter.
شافع مشفع (shafi' mushaffa'): An intercessor whose intercession is accepted.

Who is Most Entitled to Lead the Janazah Prayer
Order of precedence for leading the funeral prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of precedence for leading the janazah prayer and explain why the caliph is most entitled.

Core Idea
The caliph must lead the janazah prayer; giving precedence to anyone else is disrespectful.

In this lesson, we examine a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi's hashiya on the proper etiquette for the janazah prayer. The source passage clarifies that the caliph (supreme ruler) has the primary right to lead, and that this is not merely recommended but obligatory due to the respect due to him. The term 'sunnah' in this context is explained as the established religious practice, not a mere recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the most entitled person
Read the phrase 'al-sultan ahaqqu bi salatihi' and note that the sultan is defined as the caliph, the head of state.
2
Understand the reason
The text states 'li wujubi ta'zimihi' – giving precedence to someone else would be a humiliation, so it is wajib to honor the caliph by letting him lead.
This is a talil (causal reasoning).
3
Recognize the next in order
The caliph's deputy (na'ib), who is the city governor, is next entitled. The text says giving him precedence is also obligatory and is the 'sunnah'.
Deputy means the representative in political matters.
4
Clarify the term 'sunnah'
The commentator explains that 'sunnah' here refers to the established normative practice (al-tariqa al-ma'huda fi al-din), not merely a recommended act. This resolves any apparent contradiction with the obligatory nature.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالتنوين قوله : (السلطان أحق بصلاته) المراد بالسلطان الخليفة. قوله: (لواجب تعظيمه) أي لتعظيمه الواجب لأن في تقديم غيره عليه إهانته قوله : (ثم نائبه) أي نائب الخليفة في أحكام السياسة، وهو أمير البلدة كما في الدرر ويجب تقديمه، ولا ينافيه قوله لأنه السنة لأن المراد بها في كلامه الطريقة المعهودة في الدين قوله : ( لأنه السنة) أي لأن تقديم النائب
With tanwin. His statement: 'The sultan is most entitled to his prayer' — what is meant by sultan is the caliph. His statement: 'due to the obligation of honoring him' i.e., his obligatory respect, because giving precedence to someone else over him is a humiliation. His statement: 'then his deputy' i.e., the deputy of the caliph in matters of political rule, and he is the governor of the city, as in al-Durar, and giving him precedence is obligatory. This does not contradict his statement 'because it is sunnah' because what is meant by sunnah in his speech is the established way in the religion. His statement: 'because it is sunnah' i.e., because giving precedence to the deputy is the sunnah.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This is a critical refinement from al-Tahtawi's hashiya on the ruling of who is most entitled to lead the janazah prayer. The matn states that the sultan (caliph) is most entitled to lead it, due to the obligation of honoring him; giving precedence to someone else would be disrespectful. Next in order is his deputy (na'ib), i.e., the governor of the city, because that is the sunnah (established practice). The commentator clarifies that the sultan here means the caliph (khalifah), not just any ruler. The phrase 'due to the obligation of honoring him' means respecting the caliph is obligatory, and prioritizing someone else over him would be an insult. The deputy is the caliph's representative in political matters, such as the city governor. His precedence is also obligatory, and this does not contradict the statement 'because it is sunnah' because 'sunnah' here refers to the established religious practice, not merely a recommended act. This order of precedence is part of the proper etiquette for janazah prayer.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultan): The caliph (khalifah), the supreme ruler.
السنة (al-sunnah): The established religious practice, not just the recommended acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Order of Those Entitled to Lead Funeral Prayer
States the hierarchy of who leads the janazah prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of those entitled to lead the janazah prayer and apply the reasoning for the precedence of the sultan, his deputy, and the imam over the wali.

Core Idea
The sultan and his deputy are wajib to lead; the imam of the neighborhood is preferred over the wali if better.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the hierarchy of who leads the funeral prayer. It distinguishes between obligatory precedence (sultan, deputy, qadi) and recommended preference (imam of the neighborhood). The ruling also involves an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wali versus imam, and the father versus son.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Officials and Their Order
List the persons in order: sultan, his deputy (emir), qadi, chief of police, deputy of governor, deputy of judge, then imam of the neighborhood, then wali.
The first four are political/judicial authorities.
2
Determine Wajib vs Mandub Precedence
Presenting the sultan and his deputy (and by extension other officials) is wajib to avoid disrespect. Presenting the imam of the neighborhood is mandub only if he is better than the wali.
The text uses 'wajib' for sultan and deputy.
3
Analyze the Dalil – Sunnah of al-Husayn
The practice of al-Husayn presenting Sa'id ibn al-'As (the governor) to lead the prayer of Hasan is cited as proof that the ruler should lead.
This is a sunnah (practice) of a Companion, a valid source in Hanafi.
4
Understand the Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Wali vs Imam
Abu Yusuf holds that the wali is more entitled because it is a guardianship matter like marriage. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say the imam of the neighborhood is first if better, due to the deceased's satisfaction.
The correct view (sahih) is the majority.
5
Distinguish Father vs Son Priority
Although the general order of 'usubah in marriage puts sons before fathers, for janazah the father is presented over the son obligatorily to show respect. There is disagreement, but the mufta bihi is father first.
This is based on the father's virtue and avoiding disrespect.

His statement: (The sultan is more entitled to his prayer) meaning the caliph. His statement: (Due to the obligation of honoring him) i.e., due to his obligatory reverence, because presenting others before him shows disrespect. His statement: (Then his deputy) i.e., the deputy of the caliph in matters of political rule, and he is the emir of the town as in al-Durar, and his precedence is obligatory. And it does not contradict his statement 'because it is the sunnah,' because what is meant by it in his speech is the established way in religion. His statement: (because it is the sunnah) i.e., because presenting the deputy... The chief of police, then the deputy of the governor, then the deputy of the judge (then the imam of the neighborhood) because he was satisfied with him in his life, so he is more entitled than the wali according to the correct view. (Then the male wali) who is accountable, so no right for the woman, minor, or insane person. The closest is prioritized in order, like their order in marriage, but the father is presented over the son according to all, by God, on the correct view due to his virtue. And the shaykh of my teachers...
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This is a passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah, providing a critical refinement of the ruling on who is most entitled to lead the janazah prayer. The passage begins by clarifying that 'sultan' here means the caliph, and his precedence is obligatory to avoid disrespect. Next, the caliph's deputy (the emir of the town) is presented because it is the sunnah (established practice). Then the qadi, due to his general authority. Then comes the chief of police (sahib al-shurtah), then the deputy of the governor (khalifah al-wali), then the deputy of the judge. After these officials, the imam of the neighborhood is presented if he is better than the wali, but this is recommended (mandub) not obligatory. The wali (guardian) is the one responsible for the deceased, and his precedence follows the order of 'usubah in marriage: first sons, then fathers, then brothers, then uncles, etc. However, the father is presented over the son obligatorily because presenting the son shows disrespect to the father. There is an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Yusuf holds that the wali is more entitled because the ruling pertains to guardianship like marriage, while Imam Muhammad and others hold the view mentioned. The relied-upon view is that the father precedes the son.

Key Terms
السلطان (al-sultan): Here specifically the caliph, the supreme ruler.
النائب (al-na'ib): The deputy of the caliph in political matters, e.g., the emir of the town.
إمام الحي (imam al-hayy): The imam of the neighborhood mosque, as distinct from the judge or political rulers.
الولي (al-wali): The guardian of the deceased, specifically a male relative who is accountable (mukallaf) and in order of 'usubah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, who is presented first in leading the funeral prayer among the following?
A) The wali (guardian)
B) The imam of the neighborhood
C) The deputy of the caliph (na'ib)
D) The chief of police (sahib al-shurtah)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi hierarchy for leading janazah prayer prioritizes political and judicial authority (wajib) over local imams and guardians, with the father preceding the son.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Hierarchy of Entitlement to Lead Funeral Prayer
Details the hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi hierarchy of who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer, identify the proof and the intra-madhhab disputes, and apply the ruling to a scenario.

Core Idea
The ruler's deputy leads the funeral prayer as an obligation; the guardian's right is secondary but can be delegated.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies the precise order of entitlement to lead the funeral prayer. It distinguishes between obligatory precedence (ruler and his deputies) and recommended precedence (imam of the neighborhood), and details the order of guardians who may lead in their absence. Understanding this hierarchy prevents disorder and ensures the prayer is led by the most appropriate person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling and its categories
The passage classifies entitlement into two types: wajib (obligatory) for the ruler/deputy, and mustahabb (recommended) for the imam of the neighborhood. The guardian's right is a personal right that can be waived.
Not all persons have equal status: the presence of the ruler imposes an obligation.
2
Trace the explicit hierarchy
The order is: Sultan (ruler) → his deputy (sahib al-shart) → governor's deputy → judge's deputy → imam of the neighborhood → guardian (wali) in order of closeness (as in marriage).
The 'sahib al-shart' is the chief of police, a deputy of the ruler.
3
Analyze the dalil
The passage cites the hadith of Abu Hurairah about three answered supplications to support the father's precedence over the son: the parent's supplication is more likely to be answered, so the father leading benefits the deceased.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for the ruling.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf holds that the guardian (wali) is more entitled than the ruler's deputy, analogizing to marriage. Abu Hanifa says the ruler's deputy is preferred to avoid fasad (disorder). The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's.
Also, regarding father vs. son: Abu Hanifa says father is wajib; Muhammad says son is preferred in some transmissions, but the relied-upon is father.
5
Apply the rules of delegation and multiple guardians
The one entitled may permit another to lead. If two equal guardians are present, the second can prevent the first's delegate. The elder's choice is given precedence.
These details ensure order when multiple eligible persons are present.

Book of Prayer. The owner of the mark (sahib al-shart) is the deputy of the governor, then the deputy of the judge, then the imam of the neighborhood because he was pleased with him in his lifetime, so he is more entitled than the guardian according to the correct view. Then the male guardian who is legally responsible; so no right for a woman, a minor, or an insane person. The closest is given precedence then the next closest, like their order in marriage, but the father is given precedence over the son in the saying of all, for his virtue... And the master is more entitled than the relative of his slave according to the correct view, and the relative is given precedence over the emancipator. If there is no guardian, then the husband, then the neighbors. And whoever has the right of precedence may permit another, because he can abandon his right. If there are multiple [with equal right], the second can prevent. The one presented by the elder is more entitled than the one presented by the younger...
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This is a commentary from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah, critically refining the rulings on who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer. The passage opens by defining the hierarchy: first the ruler (sultan), then his deputy (sahib al-shart/chief of police), then the governor's deputy, then the judge's deputy, then the imam of the neighborhood. The commentary notes that the sultan's precedence is wajib if present, while the imam of the neighborhood is mustahabb. It then discusses the guardians (awliya): the male, mature, sane relative is entitled, with order same as in marriage (son, then father, then brother, etc.), but the father is preferred over the son even if the son is more learned, due to the father's virtue. A hadith is cited that three supplications are answered: the oppressed, the traveller, and the parent for their child. Then it covers cases like the master of a slave, the husband, and neighbors. It also discusses that the one entitled may delegate another, but if there are two equals, the second can prevent the first's delegate. The commentary ends with details on multiple guardians and the preference of the elder's choice.

Key Terms
صاحب الشرط (sahib al-shart): The chief of police or the one in charge of security, who has a distinct mark (shart) of authority.
الولي (al-wali): The guardian of the deceased, i.e., the closest male relative responsible for burial arrangements.
إمام الحي (imam al-hayy): The imam of the neighborhood mosque, who is entitled to lead if he is better than the guardian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, who is most entitled to lead the funeral prayer if the ruler is present?
A) The father of the deceased
B) The son of the deceased
C) The ruler or his deputy
D) The imam of the neighborhood mosque

Key Takeaway
The ruler's deputy leads the funeral prayer as an obligation; the father leads only when no ruler or deputy is present; the imam leads as a recommended act if he is more virtuous.

Repeating Funeral Prayer by the Rightful Guardian
Commentary on the ruling when another prays without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on repeating the funeral prayer when another prays without permission, and identify the conditions under which repetition is permissible.

Core Idea
The rightful guardian may repeat the funeral prayer if another led without permission—but it is optional, not obligatory.

In this passage, al-Tahtawi comments on a key ruling from Maraqi al-Falah: when someone other than the rightful guardian leads the janazah prayer without permission, the guardian has the option to repeat the prayer. However, this repetition is not obligatory. The commentary clarifies the conditions, resolves apparent contradictions with the Prophet's practice, and refutes a stronger view from al-Taqwim. By the end, you will understand the precise legal scenario and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is repeating the funeral prayer. The ruling: it is permissible (mubah) if the rightful person chooses, not wajib.
2
Locate the conditions for permissibility
What triggers the option? When someone other than the rightful person prays without permission and the rightful person does not follow as ma'moom.
3
Analyse the exceptions
When is repetition not allowed? If the rightful person gave permission or followed the prayer, his right drops. Also if multiple guardians, only one may pray.
4
Examine the proof and its limitation
The Prophet's prayer over a man buried after his guardian's prayer is cited. But this was a special right; for others, consensus forbids repetition after the guardian's prayer.
5
Evaluate the alternative view
The commentary rejects al-Taqwim's position that the obligation remains on the rightful person. Understand why this view is considered weak.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: ( فإن صلى غيره الخ ) شمل ما إذا صلى عليه ولى القرابة، وأراد السلطان أن يصلي عليه فله ذلك لأنه مقدم عليه كما في الجوهرة يعني إذا كان حاضراً وقت الصلاة، ولم يصل مع الولي، ولم يأذن لاتفاق كلمتهم على أنه لا حق للسلطان عند عدم حضوره نهر. قوله: بلا إذن ولم يقتد به أما إذا أذن له، أو لم يأذن، ولكن صلى خلفه، فليس له أن يعيد لأنه سقط حقه بالأذن أو بالصلاة مرة وهي لا تتكرر، ولو صلى عليه الولي، وللميت أولياء آخرون بمنزلته ليس لهم أن يعيدوا لأن ولاية الذي صلى متكاملة. قوله: (أعادها) ولو على قبره كذا في الدر. قوله : (هو) إنما ذكر الضمير لأنه لو حذفه لتوهم عود الضمير في على الغير قوله : (إن شاء) أي فالإعادة ليست بواجبة قوله : (وإن تأدى الفرض بها أي بصلاة غيره أشار به وبالتخيير إلى ضعف ما في التقويم من أنه لو صلى غير ذي الحق كانت الصلاة باقية على ذي الحق والي ردماً في الإتقان من أن الأمر موقوف إن أعاد ذو الحق تبين أن الفرض ما صلى، وإلا سقط بالأولى قوله لأنّ التنقل بها غير مشروع ولعدم حقه . قوله: (كما لا يصلي أحد عليها بعده وإن صلى وحده) وصلاة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على من دفن بعد صلاة وليه عليه لحق تقدمه مطلقاً، وصلاة الصحابة عليه أفواجاً خصوصية كما أن تأخير الأثنين إلى ليلة الأربعاء كان كذلك لأنه مكروه في حق غيره بالإجماع، أو لأنها كانت فرض عين على الصحابة لعظيم حقه عليهم لا تنفلاً بها وألا يصلى على قبره الشريف إلى يوم القيامة لبقائه كما دفن طرياً، بل هو حي يرزق ويتنعم بسائر الملاذ والعبادات وكذا سائر الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، وقد أجمعت الأمة على تركها كما في السراج والحلبي والشرح
His saying: (If someone other [than the rightful person] prays, etc.) includes the case where a relative with guardianship prays, and the sultan wants to pray over him; he may do so because he has precedence over him, as in al-Jawharah. Meaning, if he is present at the time of prayer and did not pray with the guardian and did not give permission, because they agreed that the sultan has no right when he is absent. Al-Nahr. His saying: 'without permission and not following him' – but if he gave him permission, or did not give permission but prayed behind him, he may not repeat, because his right is dropped by permission or by praying once, which is not repeated. And if the guardian prayed, and the deceased has other guardians of the same rank, they may not repeat, because the guardianship of the one who prayed is complete. His saying: 'he repeats' even over his grave, as in al-Durr. His saying: 'he' – he mentioned the pronoun because if he omitted it, one might think the pronoun referred back to 'other'. His saying: 'if he wishes' – i.e., the repetition is not obligatory. His saying: 'even if the obligation is fulfilled by it' – i.e., by the prayer of another. He indicated by this and by the choice the weakness of what is in al-Taqwim, that if someone other than the rightful person prays, the prayer remains incumbent on the rightful person. And he replied in al-Itqan that the matter is suspended: if the rightful person repeats, it becomes clear that the obligation was performed by his prayer, otherwise it is dropped by the first. His saying: 'because performing supererogatory prayer with it is not legitimate' and due to his lack of right. His saying: 'just as no one may pray over him after him, even if he prays alone' – and the prayer of the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) over someone buried after his guardian had prayed was due to his absolute precedence, and the prayer of the Companions over him in groups was a special characteristic, just as delaying the two to Tuesday night was likewise, because it is disliked for others by consensus, or because it was an individual obligation on the Companions due to his great right over them, not by way of supererogatory prayer. And otherwise, prayer over his noble grave would be offered until the Day of Resurrection because he remains as he was buried fresh, rather he is alive, sustained, and enjoying all pleasures and acts of worship, and likewise all the prophets (peace be upon them). The ummah has unanimously abandoned it, as in al-Siraj, al-Halabi, and al-Sharh.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (hashiya) on a ruling from Maraqi al-Falah regarding the funeral prayer. The ruling states that if someone other than the rightful person (such as a relative guardian or the sultan) prays over the deceased without the rightful person's permission and without the rightful person following as a ma'moom, then the rightful person may repeat the prayer if he wishes. The repetition is not obligatory but optional. The commentary clarifies several points: (1) If the sultan is present and the guardian prays without his permission, the sultan may pray over the deceased again because he has precedence; (2) If the rightful person gives permission or prays behind the one leading, he cannot repeat because his right is dropped; (3) If one guardian prays, other guardians of equal rank cannot repeat because the guardianship of the one who prayed is complete; (4) The repetition can be performed even over the grave after burial. The commentary also provides the rationale: performing supererogatory prayer on a funeral is not legitimate, and no one may pray over the deceased after the rightful person has prayed, as illustrated by the Prophet's practice. The Prophet once prayed over a man who was buried after his guardian had prayed, but this was due to his special precedence. The Companions also prayed over the Prophet in groups, but this was a special case. For ordinary people, the funeral prayer is not repeated after the guardian has prayed, by consensus.

Key Terms
التنفل (al-tanafful): Performing a supererogatory (nafl) prayer. Here, it is stated that performing a supererogatory funeral prayer (i.e., repeating it without a rightful cause) is not legitimate.
الولي (al-wali): The guardian of the deceased, typically a close relative (e.g., father, son, brother) who has the primary right to lead the funeral prayer.
الإعادة (al-i'adah): Repetition; here, the act of performing the funeral prayer again after it has already been performed by someone else.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the rightful person repeating the funeral prayer if someone else prayed without his permission and without him following?
A) It is obligatory (wajib).
B) It is prohibited (haram).
C) It is optional (mubah) if he wishes.
D) It is recommended (sunnah).

Key Takeaway
The rightful guardian may optionally repeat the janazah prayer if another led without permission, but the obligation is fulfilled by the first prayer.

Guardian vs Appointee in Leading Funeral Prayer
Commentary on guardian's precedence over appointee in funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on the validity of a bequest for leading funeral prayer and explain why the guardian's right overrides the bequest.

Core Idea
A deceased's bequest for a funeral prayer leader is invalid; the guardian's shari'i right prevails.

This lesson examines the conflict between a deceased's will (wasiyyah) and the shari'i right of the guardian (wali) in leading the funeral prayer. You will learn the mufta bihi position that the bequest is invalid, and how the guardian retains precedence even according to a minority view that upholds the bequest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Competing Claims
Recognize the two parties: the guardian (who holds wilāyah) and the person appointed by the deceased's bequest. The guardian claims precedence based on shari'ah, while the appointee claims it based on the will.
The text explicitly contrasts 'the one who has guardianship of precedence' with 'the one to whom the deceased bequeathed'.
2
Determine the Muftā Bihī Ruling
The text states 'الوصية باطلة على المفتي به' — the bequest is invalid according to the relied-upon position. This is the ruling to follow in practice.
Al-Sadr al-Shahid is cited as the authority for this position.
3
Recognize the Intra-Madhhab Divergence
Contrast the muftā bihī with the narration from Ibn Rustam in the Nawādir, which holds the bequest permissible (jā'iz).
This divergence shows the range of transmissions within the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the Practical Outcome
Even according to Ibn Rustam's view, the guardian is still given precedence over the appointee. The commentator clarifies: 'ومع ذلك يقدم من له حق التقدم' — even so, the one with the right of precedence is given precedence.
Thus, both views agree on the final action, differing only on the status of the bequest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ومن له ولاية التقدم فيها أحق بالصلاة عليها) ممن أوصى له الميت بالصلاة عليه لأن الوصية باطلة على المفتي به قاله الصدر الشهيد وفي نوادر ابن رستم الوصية جائزة قال في القاموس: رستم بضم الراء وفتح المثناة فوق وقد تضم اسم جماعة محدثين والرستميون جماعة ا هـ . قوله: (الوصية جائزة) أي ومع ذلك يقدم من له حق التقدم
His saying: 'And the one who has guardianship of precedence in it is more entitled to pray over it' than the one to whom the deceased bequeathed that he pray over him, because the bequest is invalid according to the fatwa (mufta bihi). Al-Sadr al-Shahid said so. And in the Nawadir of Ibn Rustam, the bequest is permissible. He said in al-Qamus: Rustam with damma on ra and fatha on the second letter, and it may be with damma, the name of a group of hadith scholars, and the Rustamiyoon are a group. End. His saying: 'the bequest is permissible' meaning, even so, the one who has the right of precedence is given precedence.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling that the person who holds guardianship (wilayah) for leading the funeral prayer—typically the nearest male relative—is more entitled to lead than a person who was appointed by the deceased's will. The reason given is that such a bequest is invalid (batil) according to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position. However, there is a divergent narration from Ibn Rustam that the bequest is valid (ja'iz). Despite this difference, the commentator clarifies that even if the bequest is considered valid, the one with the right of precedence (the guardian) is still given priority. This is consistent with the Hanafi principle that the guardian's right is based on shari'i authority, whereas a bequest is a personal choice that cannot override the established order.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A bequest made by the deceased requesting a specific person to lead his funeral prayer. The text discusses its validity.
الولي (al-walī): The guardian who has the right to lead the funeral prayer, typically the nearest male relative (e.g., son, father, brother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the muftā bihī (relied-upon) position, what is the status of a bequest appointing someone to lead the funeral prayer?
A) It is valid and must be followed.
B) It is invalid (bāṭil).
C) It is recommended (mustaḥabb).
D) It is disliked (makrūh).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the guardian's right to lead funeral prayer overrides any bequest; the bequest is generally invalid according to the mufta bihi.

Prayer over the Grave: Ruling and Conditions
Ruling with proof using istihsan and conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on offering funeral prayer over a grave after burial without prior washing, and identify when decomposition prevents it.

Core Idea
Prayer over a grave is permitted by istihsan even without washing, but only if burial is complete and the body has not decomposed.

This lesson examines the scenario where a deceased person is buried without the funeral prayer. The passage clarifies that if earth has been poured over the grave, prayer may be offered over the grave even without washing, based on the principle of istihsan (juristic preference). It also explains the critical condition of decomposition and the reliance on the dominant opinion (akbar al-ra'y) to determine it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and ruling
Understand that the passage deals with a person buried without prayer or washing due to a reason (e.g., forgetfulness). The ruling is that prayer is offered over the grave if earth has been poured.
The Arabic phrase 'صلي على قبره' indicates the act.
2
Understand the rationale: istihsan
Why is prayer allowed without washing? Because exhuming the body is prohibited (haram) after earth is poured. Washing is impossible, so the obligation is fulfilled as much as possible by praying at the grave. This is istihsan overriding strict analogy.
The text says 'على المعتمد، وهو الاستحسان'.
3
Note the condition: earth poured vs. not poured
If earth has not been poured (burial incomplete), the body is exhumed, washed, and prayed over normally. If earth is poured, exhumation is forbidden.
The text distinguishes between 'أهيل عليه التراب' and 'لم يهل التراب'.
4
Recognize the decomposition limit
Even if burial is complete, if the body has decomposed (tafasukha), prayer cannot be offered. Decomposition means limbs separate. The criterion is the dominant opinion (akbar al-ra'y) considering time, climate, and body condition. Doubt about decomposition prevents prayer.
The text says 'ما لم يتفسخ' and 'فلو شك في تفسخه لا يصلى عليه'.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., Ghayat al-Bayan) prohibit prayer without washing, but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) allows it by istihsan. The commentary supports the istihsan view.
The text says 'وصحح في غاية البيان منع الصلاة في هذه الحالة' and 'على المعتمد'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وإن دفن) وأهيل عليه التراب بلا صلاة لأمر اقتضى ذلك صلي على قبره وإن لم يغسل لسقوط شرط طهارته لحرمة نبشه وتعاد لو صلي عليه قبل الدفن بلا غسل لفساد الأولى بالقدرة على تغسيله قبل الدفن وقيل تنقلب صحيحة لتحقق العجز ولو لم يهل التراب يخرج فيغسل ويصلى عليه ما لم يتفسخ والمعتبر فيه أكبر الرأي على الصحيح لاختلافه باختلاف الزمان والإنسان . قوله: (الأمر اقتضى ذلك) من نسيان، وغيره والأولى حذفه لإيهامه أنه إذا كان لجهل يخرج، ويصلى عليه وليس كذلك لأن العلة عامة . قوله: (صلى على قبره) إقامة للواجب بقدر الإمكان كذا في التبيين قوله : (وإن لم يغسل) على المعتمد، وهو الاستحسان، وصحح في غاية البيان منع الصلاة في هذه الحالة لأنها لم تشرع بدون غسل، ولو وضع الميت لغير القبلة، أو على شقه الأيسر، أو جعل رأسه في موضع رجليه وأهيل عليه التراب لم ينبش ولو سوى عليه اللبن، ولم يهيلوا عليه التراب ينزع اللبن وتراعي السنة كذا في التبيين وهذا يؤيد تقييد الكمال بإهالة التراب، ويرد ما في الخلاصة قوله: (لتحقق العجز) أي الشرعي لا العقلي. قوله : (ما لم يتفسخ) أي تفرق أعضاؤه فإن تفسخ لا يصلى عليه مطلقاً لأنها شرعت على البدن، ولا وجود له مع التفسخ، وأما صلاته الله على شهداء أحد بعد ثمان سنين على ما رواه البخاري عن عقبة بن عامر، فمحمول على الدعاء، أو لأنهم لم يتفسخوا فإنّ معاوية لما أراد تحويلهم ليجري العين التي بأحد عند قبور الشهداء وجدهم كما دفنوا حتى أن المسحاة أصابت إصبع حمزة رضي الله عنه، فانفطرت دماً فتركهم أو هو خصوصية له وتمامه في شرح المشكاة. قوله: (والمعتبر فيه) أي في التفسخ. قوله : (أكبر (الرأي فلو شك في تفسخه لا يصلى عليه كما في النهر عن محمد، وكأنه تقديم للمانع سيد عن الدر. قوله : (باختلاف الزمان) برداً وحراً، والمكان رخاوة، وصلابة قوله : (والإنسان) أي الميت سمناً، وهزالاً ا هـ سيد عن مسكين.
His saying: 'And if he is buried' and earth is poured over him without prayer due to a reason that necessitated that, prayer is offered over his grave even if he was not washed, because the condition of his purification is dropped due to the prohibition of exhuming him. And it is repeated if prayer was offered over him before burial without washing, due to the invalidity of the first prayer since washing him was possible before burial. And it is said that it becomes valid due to the existence of inability. And if earth was not poured over him, he is taken out, washed, and prayed over, unless he has decomposed (tafasakha). And the consideration in that is the dominant opinion (akbar al-ra'y) according to the correct view, due to its variation with time and person. His saying: 'the reason necessitated that' – from forgetfulness, etc. It is better to omit it because it implies that if it was due to ignorance, he would be taken out and prayed over, which is not the case because the cause is general. His saying: 'prayer is offered over his grave' – performing the obligation as much as possible, as in al-Tabyin. His saying: 'even if he was not washed' – according to the relied-upon view, which is istihsan. And in Ghayat al-Bayan, the prohibition of prayer in this case is considered correct because it was not legislated without washing. And if the deceased was placed not facing the qibla, or on his left side, or his head placed where his feet should be, and earth poured over him, he is not exhumed. And if they placed bricks over him without pouring earth, the bricks are removed and the sunnah is observed, as in al-Tabyin. This supports the restriction of al-Kamal to the pouring of earth, and rejects what is in al-Khulasah. His saying: 'due to the existence of inability' – i.e., legal inability, not rational. His saying: 'unless he has decomposed (tafasakha)' i.e., his limbs become separated. If he has decomposed, prayer is not offered over him at all, because it is legislated for the body, and there is no body with decomposition. As for the Prophet's prayer over the martyrs of Uhud after eight years, as narrated by Bukhari from Uqbah ibn Amir, it is interpreted as supplication (du'a), or because they had not decomposed. Indeed, when Muawiyah wanted to move them to run the spring at Uhud by the graves of the martyrs, he found them as they were buried, such that the shovel struck Hamzah's finger (may Allah be pleased with him) and it bled, so he left them. Or it was a special characteristic for him. The rest is in Sharh al-Mishkat. His saying: 'the consideration in it' i.e., in decomposition. His saying: 'the dominant opinion' – if there is doubt about decomposition, prayer is not offered over him, as in al-Nahr from Muhammad. It seems the preventive factor is given precedence. Sayyid from al-Durr. His saying: 'varying with time' – cold and heat, and with place – softness and hardness. His saying: 'and person' i.e., the deceased being fat or thin. End. Sayyid from Miskin.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a deceased person is buried without the funeral prayer due to a reason (e.g., forgetfulness, emergency), and the question is whether prayer can be performed over the grave. The ruling is that if earth has been poured over the grave (i.e., the burial is complete), prayer may be offered at the grave even if the deceased was not washed, because exhuming the body is prohibited (haram) after burial. The obligation of prayer is fulfilled as much as possible. However, there is an opinion that prayer without washing is invalid (from Ghayat al-Bayan), but the relied-upon view (mu'tamad) is istihsan (juristic preference) allowing it. If the earth has not been poured over the grave, the body may be exhumed, washed, and prayed over, as long as decomposition has not set in. The criterion for decomposition is the 'dominant opinion' (akbar al-ra'y) of the person in charge, considering climate and the condition of the body. If there is doubt about decomposition, prayer is not offered. The commentary also discusses related details: if the body was placed incorrectly (not facing qibla), it is not exhumed after earth is poured; if only bricks were placed, they are removed to correct the position. The hadith of the Prophet praying over the martyrs of Uhud after years is explained as either a special case (due to their lack of decomposition) or as a supplication, not a funeral prayer.

Key Terms
التفسخ (al-tafasukh): Decomposition of the body to the extent that limbs separate. If this occurs, no funeral prayer can be offered over the grave.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that permits prayer over the grave without prior washing, overriding the strict analogy (qiyas) that would require washing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on offering the janazah prayer at the grave if the deceased was buried without being washed?
A) It is not permissible because washing is a necessary condition for janazah prayer.
B) It is permissible according to the relied-upon view (istihsan), even if the body has decomposed.
C) It is permissible only if earth has been poured over the grave and the body has not decomposed.
D) It is obligatory to exhume and wash the body first.

Key Takeaway
After burial, the janazah prayer over the grave is permitted by istihsan even without washing, provided earth is poured and no decomposition has occurred; doubt about decomposition prevents the prayer.
